Current Affairs Commentary

The Restoration of the Pre-War International Situation 15

— Hua

The recent development of international relations has a tendency to gradually revert to the pre-war situation. The amity between France and the Soviet Union, the cooperation between Britain and France, the secret military alliance between Germany and Japan, and the gradual formation of a united Anglo-American front are all obvious signs. Although the composition of this combination differs somewhat from that before the First World War, the fundamental approach is the same: the opposition of the balance of power becomes increasingly intense, and the division of the lines of battle becomes more obvious. As soon as the balance of power is broken in one corner, the entire line can be affected and erupt into a pan-global war. The development of this situation has far-reaching consequences, and we must pay close attention to it.

The development of international relations before the war was driven by a group of emerging imperialists who were dissatisfied with the status quo of the world's division and challenged the imperialists who originally occupied the world's advantage. At that time, the main force representing the emerging imperialists was Germany, and the main force representing the imperialists occupying the world's advantage was Britain and France. There was originally a strong struggle between Britain and France, such as the struggle for Sudan, which almost led to war. However, the crisis of the conflict between Britain and France gradually eased due to the rise of the German power. The German imperialists showed their face to the world and promoted the cooperation between Britain and France with a tough attitude. When Germany, Austria-Hungary, and Italy formed an alliance against the status quo, Britain and France and Imperial Russia conducted consultations and formed a combination to maintain the status quo. The two sides were clearly divided, and once the balance of power was broken, a full-scale war broke out.

In the decade or so after the war, the imperialists who represented the world's advantage were still Britain and France, and the United States can also be counted as one. Those who represented the new forces and were not satisfied with the status quo were Japan and Italy, which benefited from speculation during the war. Recently, the revival of German imperialism can also be attributed to this aspect. In 1931, the Japanese imperialists attacked Manchuria as the first shot to break the status quo. Last year, the Italian imperialists invaded East Africa as the second shot. Germany has reorganized its military and will demand the return of its old colonies when its strength has grown and the time is right, which will be the third shot. This kind of action to break the status quo and demand the redivision of the world was very scattered in its initial form and reaction. The United Kingdom, France, the United States, and other countries that occupy an advantage in the world cannot immediately abandon their prejudices and unite to deal with the forces against the status quo because they have various serious conflicts with each other. However, this situation will make the forces against the status quo more intense, and the strengthening of the forces against the status quo will eventually promote the union of those who maintain the status quo. Before the war, German Emperor Wilhelm expanded his power in East Africa and Morocco and repeatedly rejected Britain's advice, which eventually led to Britain and France abandoning their prejudices and forming a united front. Recently, Mussolini insisted on the invasion of East Africa, ignoring Britain's mediation, and made Britain and France abandon the suspicion accumulated over many years of vying for hegemony on the continent and established practical cooperation. In the Far East political situation, mutual suspicion between Britain and the United States was originally the same as the opposition between Britain and Russia before the war, and Britain's tolerance for Japan's invasion of the mainland was similar to Britain's secret assistance in the Russo-Japanese War. However, recently, the Japanese imperialists' unlimited aggression and their tough attitude on naval issues have made Britain impatient and intolerable and will eventually form a united front with the United States to resist. At the current stage, although the situation of cooperation between Britain and France and the unity between Britain and the United States has not yet reached sufficient strength, if Italy's attitude in Europe does not ease or further combines with another force against the status quo, Germany, and if Japan's aggression in the Far East continues to advance and even forms an alliance with Germany, the representative of European militarism, the unity of those who maintain the status quo will inevitably be further strengthened. Once these two lines are clearly divided, a great war can be triggered at any moment.

The recent restoration of the international situation to the pre-war state makes us feel that the peril of the Second World War is approaching again. The coming of a major collision will be a great calamity for small and weak nations and a good opportunity for the oppressed to seek liberation. However, the avoidance of this calamity and the application of this opportunity depend on our attention and preparation in advance.

British Foreign Secretary Eden's Speech: Efforts for Peaceful Negotiations; Not Allowing Aggressive Acts to Succeed; Unity of the League of Nations Is Essential for Strength 16

London - British Foreign Secretary Eden is scheduled to attend the League of Nations Council meeting in Geneva, representing the United Kingdom to consider the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. Today, he delivered a public speech in his constituency. This is Eden's first address to the public since assuming the position of Foreign Secretary.

Mr. Eden stated that League of Nations members should be able to make any aggressor realize that peaceful negotiations are not only the best way to eliminate despair but also the only way to succeed. Collective security cannot be easily achieved; it requires tireless work and sacrifice from all parties. Overall, 1935 saw good liaison work, but 1936 must see even closer liaison than before, and even 1937 must see even greater progress. Neither we nor any member state of the League of Nations should ever be complacent or think that we have succeeded, because the goal has not yet been achieved. The efforts we must make are very arduous, but I believe the British people will find it worthwhile to make these efforts. Britain's leadership position is an important factor in this critical situation. We must not be discouraged, but we must be realistic. I will approach this difficult task in this spirit. We must be forward-looking and not limit ourselves to the current war situation faced by the League of Nations. We must uphold two simple principles. In my view, there are two key principles: Aggressive actions must not be allowed to succeed; United action by member states of the League of Nations will form a strong and united body, sufficient to make any aggressor, today or in the future, realize that the best and only way to eliminate resentment and succeed is through peaceful negotiations, not aggression. We should move forward, ensuring that other countries attending Geneva not only agree with us in words but also work together with us in action to pursue a policy of peace, adopting all necessary methods to increase our strength so that we can achieve peace.

Collective Security System: Must Include Two Qualities: Strength and Flexibility 17

A collective security system, if it is to be effective, must have both strength and flexibility. The latter can be adapted to circumstances to eliminate some causes of war, while the former can effectively curb acts of aggression. These are two subsidiary attributes of a security system. The more certain this system is to include these two qualities, the more firmly its authority can be exerted, and the more other countries can fall within its scope. The so-called strength must depend on the extent to which member states of the League of Nations are prepared to fulfill their responsibilities according to their capabilities. If only one or two countries bear this entire burden, there can be no collective system. Furthermore, the effective establishment of a collective security system is the only way to achieve a compromise that can reduce the world's arms burden. It is a great mistake if anyone believes that the British government and people favor some countries over others. British policy does not follow likes or dislikes towards individuals or countries, but as a member of the League of Nations, it is obligated to oppose the destruction of the League's covenant. Any government or people who try to revert to power politics to undermine the collective security system and violate the League's covenant will be attacked by those who stand on the side of the collective system. The British people desire nothing more than peace, and they set their policies on the responsibility of being members of the League of Nations, in the hope that this will achieve peace.

Eden reviewed the events of the past year, stating that the most obvious facts were two: Switzerland's request to reorganize its military and the League of Nations' transformation from a position of being not respected to becoming a practical entity. The British people's only possible solution to European disputes lies in trusting united action, which strengthens their trust in the League of Nations. In 1935, the League of Nations underwent an extremely severe test, and the extent of its success cannot yet be determined. We have made progress, but we have not yet reached the end point. However, we are further ahead than generally predicted six months ago. The League of Nations Council would benefit greatly from examining past events and consolidating accomplished achievements. The valuable advantage of any effective collective security system is that it is the only path to disarmament agreements. The more complete the collective security system, the less insultable its authority will be, and the fewer difficulties there will be in obtaining disarmament agreements. Britain desires peace very much, desires to cooperate with all countries, and is willing to seize every opportunity to consolidate its friendship and understanding with the United States. I believe that disputes between countries can be resolved without resorting to war. If Europe were to experience another large-scale war, civilization would decline as a result. Sir Bryce once said, "If you do not eliminate war, then war will eliminate you." How true this is! Although 1935 had setbacks, it was ultimately a year of progress. Despite encountering various obstacles, the roots of the League of Nations have deepened. 1936 must be a year of continued effort to build on past achievements. With a spirit of compassion and strength, the League of Nations can restore peace and establish understanding between nations. (Reuters, 17th)

League of Nations Expresses Satisfaction: Two Points in Eden's Speech Worth Emphasizing 18

Geneva - Regarding British Foreign Secretary Eden's speech in his Warwick constituency yesterday, League of Nations officials have expressed satisfaction. The two points that deserve emphasis are: The British Foreign Secretary reiterated that aggressive actions must not be allowed to succeed; Britain's current policy is not limited to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, and its main objective is to maintain general European security. In addition, it has been stated that Britain's attitude at the upcoming League of Nations Council meeting will still be based on the principles of the League of Nations covenant. Although there is no clear indication of a solution to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, it can be considered satisfactory. (Havas, 18th)

League of Nations Meeting Tomorrow: Italian Representative Still to Attend; Sweden Protests to Italy over Bombing Incident 19

Rome - According to official sources, the government has appointed Aloisi, chief secretary of the Prime Minister's Office, to represent Italy at the League of Nations Council meeting on the 20th of this month. Semi-official sources state that the League of Nations Council meeting is a routine meeting, and Italy's sending a representative to attend the meeting has no special political significance. (Havas, 17th)

Geneva - The chairman of the Eighteen-Nation Committee of the League of Nations General Assembly, Portuguese representative Vasco Gonçalves, arrived here this morning. It is said that before convening the Eighteen-Nation Committee, he will consult with the Council and representatives of various member states of the Committee. (Havas, 18th)

Rome - The Swedish government previously protested to the Italian government over the destruction of a Swedish Red Cross ambulance team by Italian aircraft in the Sheluo area of Ethiopia. The Italian government has now replied, stating that the action was not intentional but an unfortunate accident, as the Italian aircraft was solely for military purposes. It further stated that while this matter is regrettable, those engaged in such activities must inevitably risk certain unavoidable dangers. (Reuters, 18th)

Geneva - The Uruguayan representative to the League of Nations in Geneva, Dr. Juanoni, lodged a serious protest with the League of Nations Council today over the interference of Soviet Russian committees in South American affairs. It is expected that the representative will present evidence proving that the Soviet Russian Third International secretly aided the recent failed Brazilian rebellion. The League of Nations Council will also consider the Soviet Russian protest against Uruguay's severance of diplomatic relations with Russia. (Reuters, 18th)

British Defense Plan: To Be Drafted Soon; Merger of Army, Navy, and Air Force Difficult to Achieve 20

London - The government's plan to reorganize its military is said to be drafted soon so that the Chancellor of the Exchequer can calculate the necessary expenses in time to include them in the budget. It is reported that the naval part of this plan intends to greatly increase the number of cruisers and build an aircraft carrier. As for the tonnage of battleships and the caliber of guns, etc., they will be determined after the naval conference ends, taking into account the qualitative restriction agreement that may be concluded at the conference. In the air force, it is planned to increase the production of aircraft, and the army will be mechanized on a large scale. (Havas, 17th)

London - At a cabinet meeting held a few days ago, the issue of merging the Army, Navy, and Air Force into a Ministry of Defense was discussed. It has now been learned that the departments concerned insist on their individual independence and are generally opposed to the proposal. However, the cabinet is still deliberating the merger plan. According to political figures, it is not yet known whether the three departments can be merged. If it is realized, the position of Minister of Defense is planned to be filled by the current Minister without Portfolio, Lord Ponsonby. It has been heard that the First Lord of the Admiralty, Lord Monsell, will be relieved of his duties for personal reasons, and Prime Minister Baldwin will appoint former Foreign Secretary Hoare to succeed him as First Lord of the Admiralty, thereby dispelling the negative impression left by Hoare's resignation last month. (Havas, 17th)

Naval Conference: Forming a Specialized Committee; Studying Details of Information Exchange 21

London - After the naval conference agreed on the main points of the program for exchanging shipbuilding procedures, it appointed a technical committee today to decide on the details. The committee has already begun work. The naval conference is scheduled to meet on Tuesday to discuss the issue of limiting the types of warships. The technical committee is composed of two members each from Britain, the United States, France, and Italy, and one member each from Canada and India. Today, it considered the Italian proposal for exchanging information, which advocated reporting the number and type of warships to be built at the beginning of each fiscal year, and then reporting the caliber, tonnage, and armor of the guns in detail six months later. Claypool, Counselor of the British Foreign Office, was elected chairman of the committee. (Reuters, 17th)

London - The General Committee of the Naval Conference, with representatives from Britain, France, Italy, and the United States, held a meeting this afternoon, which lasted for two hours. They reached agreement on three points regarding the methods of exchanging information on shipbuilding procedures proposed by Britain, France, and Italy: Each naval power should notify each other several months before starting the construction of a new warship; Before and during the notification period, each naval power does not need to consult each other; Each naval power should announce its shipbuilding program for the year at the beginning of each year. Regarding the first point, France advocated a period of six months, which Britain considered impractical. Regarding the second point, the method of mutual consultation was originally proposed by France, but the General Committee believed that it would cause unnecessary disputes and abandoned it, and decided that if necessary, opinions could be sought through normal diplomatic channels. Regarding the third point, the Technical Subcommittee held a meeting one and a half hours after the General Committee adjourned to discuss the shipbuilding procedures, which should be announced within the first four months of each year. Only the first point has not yet been resolved. The Technical Subcommittee is now scheduled to meet at 10:30 a.m. next Monday to discuss it. If the experts from various countries can reach an agreement at that time, the General Committee will meet on Tuesday to approve it and immediately begin discussing the issue of qualitative restrictions. It is generally believed that the views of the delegations of various countries at the naval conference have been clarified. The naval conference may announce a postponement within three weeks. As for inviting Germany and Russia to participate, according to our correspondent, the naval conference has not yet decided whether to invite them directly or notify them of the content of the agreement after it is concluded. (Havas, 17th)

London - The Japanese observer was not present at the meeting of the Silk Committee of the Naval Conference today. Members of the British delegation hosted a luncheon for members of the Japanese delegation at noon, during which they exchanged views on how to notify Japan if Britain, France, Italy, and the United States were to reach a draft agreement in the future. According to our correspondent, Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference has caused a great "conflict" between Britain and Japan. The main purpose of today's luncheon was to ease this feeling and the repercussions it may cause. It is now heard that members of the Japanese delegation plan to leave Britain next Wednesday. (Havas, 17th)

London - Nagano and Nagai, plenipotentiaries, hosted a luncheon for the heads of the British delegation at 1:00 p.m. on the 17th. British Chief of Naval Staff Chatfield and Counselor Claypole attended. Japanese Major General Iwashita, Acting British Ambassador Fujii, and all other attendants attended. As a result of the discussion on the issue of Japanese observers at the meeting, it was decided that Major General Iwashita and Acting Ambassador Fujii would attend the meeting as observers. (Domei News Agency, 17th)

King George of England Suffering from Bronchitis; Heart Weakness Worrisome; Famous Specialist Doctors Rush to Treat; Royal Family Members Stay by Bedside Day and Night 28

London - According to official announcements, King George of England has been suffering from bronchitis at Sandringham in recent days, and his heart has gradually shown signs of weakness, which is very worrying. Sir Dawson, the King's physician, traveled from London to Sandringham yesterday and spent the night there. According to his report, the King's bronchitis is not serious. The Prince of Wales and the Duke of York both went to Sandringham last night to visit the King. The King slept well last night. The King is currently resting in Sandringham, and he often rides out with the Duke of Kent. On Sunday, he even walked a quarter of a mile to church to participate in prayers. Those who saw him felt that his spirit was very good. The London medical community said that the use of the phrase "heart gradually showing signs of weakness" by the authorities is enough to prove the physician's concerns. The King celebrated his 70th birthday on June 3 last year. (Reuters, 18th)

London - It was learned from reliable sources at 7:00 a.m. this morning that King George of England slept relatively peacefully last night, and the situation throughout the evening was quite satisfactory. (According to the medical report released at 7:00 a.m. this morning, the King felt most uncomfortable between midnight and 2:00 a.m., but gradually returned to calm after that. It has been learned that Ms. Bullock, the King's favorite nurse, is currently attending to him in the sickroom. Home Secretary Sir Simon receives a phone call every hour to report on the King's condition. The discovery of previously unseen signs of heart weakness has shocked the country, as it was generally believed that the King's recovery from a serious illness in 1928 was due to the strength of the King's heart. It is now believed that the weakness of the King's body is due to overwork during the anniversary of his ascension to the throne last year. The Queen, the Prince of Wales, the Duke of York, and his wife

King George V's son are all currently in Gatlingham. The King is lying in a specially heated and ventilated room in the palace. This year's heavy snow came early, and the windows of the palace are like silver decorations, but most of the windows are lit up, indicating that the situation inside is very busy. It was learned today that the first decision to call in a doctor was made on Tuesday, when the King already showed signs of a cold. However, the country did not learn about this until 11:59 p.m. on Thursday, when all radio stations stopped broadcasting various programs and only broadcast news of the King's cold. (Guomin News Agency, 18th)

London - After three British physicians consulted by King George's bedside at 10:15 a.m. this morning, they issued a public statement stating that the concern for the King's condition expressed in last night's statement still exists today. The physicians will issue another statement tonight. It is heard that the physicians used oxygen on the King last night. The King's daughter and her husband have traveled from Berkshire to Sandringham Palace today to visit the King. Dr. Keyser, an internist who treated the King in 1932, arrived in Sandringham this morning and immediately met with other physicians. (Reuters, 18th)

London - The public statement on the King's condition released at 3:30 p.m. today stated that the King had slept peacefully for several hours, but the signs of heart weakness and slow blood flow have increased, which is very worrying. The public statement was signed by the physicians, including Sir Dawson. (Reuters, 18th)

British Imperial Poet Rudyard Kipling Dies; Cremation of Remains to Be Held 29

London: The famous literary giant Rudyard Kipling passed away at 12:10 last night at a hospital in Midhurst, Sussex. Kipling was admitted to the hospital late this week due to a perforated stomach ulcer. Surgeon Johnson performed an operation on the morning of the day before yesterday, but his condition did not improve. After Friday, his physical strength was completely exhausted, and he died last night. Dr. Johnson was also in the ward at the time and immediately issued a report saying, "Kipling passed away peacefully, with his wife and daughter by his side. He remained lucid throughout his illness, struggling against the disease, but ultimately succumbed and passed away." It snowed heavily last night, and the whole city was like a silver world. All was quiet in the Sussex Hospital when this famous literary giant passed away. The sad news caused widespread shock and mourning. His body is currently displayed in the hospital morgue, awaiting his family's decision on the burial site before the funeral is held. (Havas, 18th)

London: Rudyard Kipling's remains will be cremated. The time and location will be announced later. (Reuters, 18th)

New York: The Poet Laureate of the British Empire, John Masefield, is currently visiting the United States. Today, he paid high tribute to the famous British poet and writer Rudyard Kipling, saying that Kipling was indeed the best poet of the British Empire, and also a novelist of genius. His poems and prose were extremely popular, humorous, and romantic. In addition, the British novelist Hugh Walpole, currently in Los Angeles, also praised Kipling's works, saying that Kipling's writings were unique, lively, and creative, and would never be forgotten by the world. Canadian Prime Minister Sir Robert Borden, an old friend of Kipling's, said in Ottawa after hearing the sad news of Kipling's death that Kipling was the greatest figure in modern British literature. The British Empire has lost a great patriot, a great artist, and a truly loving person. (Reuters, 18th) The literary fame of the British literary giant Rudyard Kipling was widespread both domestically and internationally, and his experience was indeed a rare one for a writer. He first showed his talent at a young age, and his poems and prose were popular for a time. Before long, the French were also captivated by his writings, calling him "the last poet." He liked to travel extensively from a young age. In his works, he always praised the power of the empire, and the British called him "the poet of the empire," which was well-deserved. He was born in Bombay, India in 1865. His father, John Kipling, was a professor of architecture and sculpture and lived in Bombay. His mother, Alice MacDonald, was the daughter of a Wesleyan pastor. He was known for his humor as a child. Although his academic performance was not outstanding, he was quick-witted and talented. His coursework, although distinctive, showed no signs that he would become a world-renowned literary giant. At the age of seventeen, his father realized his talent and believed that if he could be freed from the shackles of school, he would be able to fully develop it. Kipling left school and entered the journalism industry, working as an editor for the "Civil and Military Gazette" in Lahore, India, to begin his career as a reporter. In 1885, he and his sister published a collection of poems in Lahore called "Echoes," which was unremarkable and did not gain much fame. Soon after, he published two more collections, "Departmental Ditties" and "Barrack-Room Ballads," which were slightly more appreciated. However, his poems still lacked originality. His prose was more readable. His first work, "Plain Tales from the Hills," was published in the Civil and Military Gazette, which he edited. The characteristics of a genius writer were already evident at this time. In 1889, he was ordered by the newspaper to travel the world and write dispatches for the paper, known as "Letters of Marque." Kipling benefited greatly from this trip. On the one hand, his writing skills were greatly improved, and on the other hand, his knowledge was broadened, allowing him to write more freely. His journey took him from China to Japan to the United States, and after three years, he arrived in England. The British were already familiar with his literary reputation, and people vied to meet him wherever he went. The Foreign Secretary Joseph Chamberlain even became his friend. At this time, the Poet Laureate Alfred Austin had just passed away. The British people believed that Kipling's literary fame was comparable to Austin's, and they all believed that Kipling could succeed to this prestigious position. However, he usually rejected honors and refused to accept the position. However, the title of "Poet of the British Nation" had already been bestowed upon him, and he was worthy of it. From then on, Kipling's life consisted of either traveling or living in seclusion in the small town of Rottingdean in Sussex, writing in a small room. At this time, his literary reputation was known far and wide. His books "The Jungle Book," "Kim," and "French Memories" were both literary and artistic masterpieces. Kipling's poems, although inevitably sacrificing meaning for the sake of words, and sacrificing their artistic characteristics for the sake of praising patriotism and imperial glory, were also able to break away from the stereotypes of his peers and were not bound by rules. At that time, British literary works, without the need for interpretation or annotation, were most able to cater to the psychology of the public. Perhaps no one surpassed Kipling in this regard. The British people and people all over the world called his later literary career "the work of a genius," and the reason for this was probably not outside of this. In 1892, Kipling married Caroline Balestier, an American woman. Because Kipling had lived in India for a long time, he looked like an Indian officer, his face was sunburned, dark and ruddy, his eyes were gray-brown and bright, his eyebrows were thick, and his beard was dense. When viewed from the side, his face was short. He was usually taciturn and rarely smiled. After his marriage, he had only one son, whom he loved very much. Unfortunately, he was killed in action on the Western Front in France during the Great War. There were many who praised Kipling's poetic and literary talents, but there were also those who criticized him. Some even denounced him as "a loyal servant of imperialism," and others accused him of harboring a self-aggrandizing mindset and supporting the pro-war faction. However, in all fairness, at the beginning of this century, the power of the British aristocracy was declining, and the morale of the people was low. Kipling believed that it was his duty to call for the restoration of national fortunes, and he was not to be blamed. In 1907, Kipling was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature, because at that time, those who admired literature and art could not escape a certain political or humanitarian framework. Kipling's "The Jungle Book" was selected. Although Kipling's call was not only seen in his poems and prose, last May, when King George V of England celebrated the 25th anniversary of his ascension to the throne, Kipling gave a speech at the London Club. In simple terms, he awakened the celebrating nation and urged them to pay attention to the seriousness of the international situation. Now that Kipling is gone, his voice still lingers in our ears. (Havas)

Silver Bloc Members of Congress Discuss Repealing Silver Tax; Treasury Undersecretary and Assistant Resign 32

Washington: Members of the House of Representatives from the silver-producing states of the American West today elected five representatives to discuss the possibility of stabilizing silver prices with silver bloc members of the Senate. The House representatives were ordered to discuss the bill passed by the Senate to repeal the provisions in the Silver Purchase Act that require silver merchants to obtain licenses, nationalize silver, and impose a 50% tax on silver profits. At the same time, the Treasury Department is unwilling to comment on the decline in silver prices. When asked about this matter, an official from the Treasury Department stated, "We are still implementing the provisions of the Silver Purchase Act. We cannot comment further." (Reuters, 17th)

Washington: The silver bloc members of the House of Representatives today decided to discuss with the silver bloc members of the Senate the bill proposed by Senator McCarran to abolish the 50% speculative silver profit tax, and then elected Martin as the leader of the attending members. Martin stated that there are currently no plans to increase the value of silver. However, Senator McCarran solemnly declared that we must immediately find a way to raise silver prices, and that if we treat silver as a commodity for one day, the rise and fall of silver prices will be uncertain for one day. I support swift action to make silver currency, stabilize the price of silver at $1.29 per ounce, and issue sufficient currency with silver ingots as reserves, making it a basic currency. I am very satisfied with the decision of the silver bloc members of the House of Representatives to discuss with the silver bloc members of the Senate the proposal I proposed to restore the free silver market in the United States. Representative Faddis stated that the silver bloc is currently in a commanding position. The impact of the large amount of silver stockpiled in the United States on the silver market is no different from the large amount of American wheat stored by the Federal Farm Board a few years ago. If such a situation had occurred in 1927, it might have led to a serious panic. But today, the world's currency situation is very different from the past. Faddis also reiterated his belief, clarifying the effectiveness of silver storage, stating that the basis of currency prices around the world is not gold and silver, but the value of the British paper pound. If this situation does not change, there will be no progress in the world's currency. I know that the future price of silver will have an important impact on the world's currency. (National Telegram, 17th)

Washington: Treasury Secretary Coolidge and Assistant Secretary Robert have both requested to resign. President Roosevelt has accepted their resignations today, and they will hand over their duties on February 15th. (Reuters, 17th)

Washington: Treasury officials today announced the amount of silver purchased when silver prices fell in December of last year, revealing that the Treasury is still far from the goal stipulated in the 1934 Silver Purchase Act. The Treasury stated that a total of 73,332,000 ounces of silver were purchased in the three weeks before December 27th last year. This purchase has raised the current silver reserves to a level of 1,526,594,000 ounces. The average price paid by the Treasury for this silver when the Roosevelt administration purchased it was 57 cents per ounce, while the current world silver price is lower than 50 cents. Based on the current $10,158,000,000 in gold reserves, the Treasury still needs to purchase 1,098,405,000 ounces of silver to comply with the provisions of the Silver Purchase Act, as the total amount of silver purchased should be one-fourth of the gold reserves. At the same time, the Department of Commerce reported today that a total of $10,507,829 worth of silver was imported in the week ending January 3rd, and $23,506,206 in the week ending January 10th, of which $14,768,819 came from the United Kingdom, $6,311,816 came from China, and $1,055,735 came from Japan. (National Telegram, 17th)

Wuhu Correspondence: The Construction Committee, in order to develop transportation in central Anhui and facilitate the transportation of coal from the Huainan coal mines under its jurisdiction, has actively constructed the Huainan Railway, which has now been fully completed. The railway is 220 kilometers long, starting from Tianjia'an in the Huainan mining area, passing through Chaoxian, Hefei, and Jiulonggang, and ending at Yuxikou, opposite Wuhu, on the Yangtze River. It traverses central Anhui and provides convenient and efficient passenger and freight transportation. Dock terminals will be established at the Yuxikou terminus and the Wuhu station of the Jiangnan Railway by the Wuhu Riverbank, and a ferry service will be arranged to connect and facilitate transportation across the river. Wuhu has decided to use the old wharf of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and has dispatched Li Zirong to Wuhu to conduct water level measurements and arrange pontoon boats. It is currently scheduled to open the entire line for trial traffic on the 20th of this month, selling tickets and operating passenger and freight transportation.
