Shang Zhen Discusses Henan Province's Administrative Work — Clearing Bandits, Banning Drugs, Preventing Traitors — 71

Kaifeng Correspondence: Shang Zhen, the newly appointed Chairman of the Henan Provincial Government, has been in office for over half a month since assuming his post on New Year's Day. However, the first Director of Education, Chen Fangxian, has not yet arrived from Beijing, and the Director of Finance, Yin Renxian, has not reported to his office, expressing his firm intention to resign. In effect, two of the four departments are at a standstill. Subsequently, after Shang Zhen repeatedly persuaded Yin, he reported to the office on the 10th and resumed his duties. Chen also reported to the office on the 15th to take charge. The entire organization of the provincial government has now been completed. According to Shang's discussion of future administrative policies, he stated: Henan Province has enjoyed peace for several years, and various scales are already in place. The most important thing is to implement the original plans in a practical manner. The government exists for the sake of the local people and should promote their interests and eliminate their problems. In the future, the government must adopt local opinions and properly plan for the welfare of the people. The current issues that should be addressed in Henan Province are:

Eradicating the remnants of bandits: Only by eliminating violence can we ensure the safety of the good people. Recently, scattered bandits in northern and western Henan have gradually gathered and harmed the local residents. A fundamental elimination must be carried out to maintain public security.

Eliminating drugs: Drugs in Henan Province are causally related to bandits. The elimination of bandits also requires the elimination of drugs.

Preventing traitors: Traitors harm the country, harbor bandits, transport drugs, and commit all kinds of evils. Therefore, it is necessary to effectively prevent them.

Other measures, such as reducing the burden on the people, are being planned. He also ordered the various departments to draft administrative steps in order to formulate procedures and seek administrative efficiency without being rash or lax. (January 16th)

Chaoshan: Large Quantities of Smuggled Goods Intercepted — A Certain Police Station Even Arrests People in Shantou — 72

Shantou Correspondence: Recently, the anti-smuggling work in Chaoshan has been extremely strict, but smugglers, with their special connections, have not reduced their activities. On the 9th, the customs patrol ship "Lianxing" patrolled the waters around Nanao and other places, and spotted a sharp-nosed speedboat heading towards Waisha in Chenghai, apparently about to unload smuggled goods. The Lianxing pursued and caught the vessel, which was identified as the "Ruixiang Maru," arriving from Taiwan. It carried 450 bags of white sugar, 450 barrels of alcohol, and seven Taiwanese ruffians. The patrol ship towed the smuggled goods and smugglers back to the Customs House for detention and investigation. When towed into Shantou Port, the authorities, fearing a raid by the ruffians, dispatched armed customs soldiers to guard the area near the Customs House. Furthermore, the Chaoshan Anti-Smuggling Office has recently been paying close attention to smuggled goods in various market towns in the Chaoshan-Meizhou inland areas. The office dispatched inspector Ye Tianyi on the 9th, leading forty to fifty special agents and tax police in three motorboats to search various rice and bean shops in Chaoyang City. However, due to a leak, the unscrupulous merchants had already moved the smuggled goods when the inspector arrived. Moreover, on the 4th, anti-smuggling officers in Jieyang District led tax police to search the markets in Fengkou, Quxi, and Paotai, seizing twenty cans of soybean oil at the Pujie Railway Station on the 7th, sixteen bags of smuggled beans in Denggang on the 8th, and over seventy bags of smuggled beans in Yugao on the 9th. On the 9th, a boat carrying smuggled goods was intercepted on the river near Paotai, containing large quantities of foreign sugar, sea cucumber, fish maw, and other goods. When the tax police detained the boat, the smuggler Lin Jing even injured a tax policeman. Statistics show that since the unified crackdown began on December 1st in the Chaoshan-Meizhou area, a large number of untaxed goods have been seized, dealing a major blow to ruffians and smugglers. Recently, they have suddenly turned their anger on the Chinese. At 11 a.m. on the 9th, a police chief from a certain consulate, accompanied by more than ten ruffians carrying short guns, arrived at No. 37, Taiping Road, third floor, and arrested Chen Zhong. Chen is from Huizhou, 29 years old. His father and brothers have been doing business in a certain place for a long time, but Chen himself has not obtained citizenship in that country. He recently worked for a certain commercial firm and has not engaged in any illegal activities. The ruffians accused Chen of leaking certain secrets and were determined to obtain them. However, Chen resisted fiercely when arrested and fled into the First District Public Security Bureau. The ruffians rushed into the branch bureau to arrest him. Chief of the branch bureau, Lu Qing, immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau and requested instructions on how to handle the situation. At that time, the police chief of a certain consulate led the ruffians in a threatening manner, claiming that Chen Zhong was impersonating a citizen of that country, investigating information, and leaking secrets, and insisted on arresting him. Chief Lu sternly refused, stating that Chen was a Chinese citizen and should be dealt with according to proper procedures if he had committed any illegal acts. Such unauthorized arrests would undermine diplomatic relations and trample on Chinese sovereignty. The ruffians had no choice but to leave in disappointment. Chen Zhong narrowly escaped. The Shantou Municipal Government submitted a letter of protest to the consul of that country on the 10th and telegraphed the details to the provincial government.

Xiang River Embankment Restoration Project Begins; 60,000 Workers Repair Yaodi in San Si Gong; Closure Work to Begin This Month, Joining Next Month 73

Hankou Correspondence: The restoration project of the Jianghan Embankment will either combine the Xiang River line into a lake or divert it into a river. The Yaodi, a flood defense levee, in the fertile area will undertake the work of closing the breaches and diverting the flow, with a budget of over 2 million yuan, originally estimated to employ 80,000 workers daily and be completed within five months. However, due to the difficulty in recruiting workers, the number has been reduced to 60,000 workers daily, recruited by the Sixth District Administrative Inspectorate Commissioner's Office, which established the Xiang River Embankment Project Office to oversee the work. Work has officially begun. Xi Dejiong, Director of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau and concurrently Director of the Xiang River Embankment Project Office, reported the progress and difficulties to Governor Yang Yongtai on the 17th. Regarding the equipment and layout, he elaborated on several points:

Worker Housing: For the Yaodi project, it is estimated that 60,000 workers are needed, requiring two reed mats per person, totaling 120,000 mats, which were purchased last December. Over 90,000 mats have been distributed and erected, accommodating 40,000 to 50,000 people. The remaining mats can be erected quickly to accommodate all 60,000 workers.

Water Pumps: Two 4-horsepower, 4-inch diameter water pumps, twenty hand-operated water pumps, and ten old-style waterwheels have been installed. A portion was transported here on December 30th of last year, and more engine-driven water pumps are being ordered to alleviate the emergency. As workers arrive, both drainage and earth filling will be carried out to prevent water from seeping back from other areas.

Erosion of Embankment Base and Ramming Seabed: Removing the turf from the embankment base and ramming the seabed have been contracted out in sections since December 5th of last year and have been completed.

Worker Food Supply: 10,000 shi of rice have been purchased in areas with abundant rice production and low prices and stored at the project site in anticipation of local rice price increases or shortages, allowing workers to purchase food freely.

Project Site Telephone: A long-distance telephone line has been negotiated with the Director of the Construction Department to be erected along the route and connected to the Shayang provincial line. Approval has also been granted by the Economic Commission to request the Ministry of Communications to dispatch personnel to establish a wireless radio station and install it in Hubei as soon as possible.

Sanitation: One or two medical teams have been established and arrived at Jiukou on January 5th.

The plan for closing the breach and the urgency of labor for the Yaodi were outlined, stating that the breach at San Si Gong is five to six kilometers long. Water rushes in through the breach, either forming a lake or dividing into several streams, with varying depths and complex conditions. In addition to the Yaodi project, the Project Office should also carry out the work of closing the breach and diverting the flow. If the flow diversion work is not done carefully, it may waste significant funds and be counterproductive. The Bureau first dispatched a survey team to conduct a detailed survey of the terrain and another team to work with the Project Office to select the Xiongjiaqiao

Page 10

to Xinjiekou section, where the river channel is narrowest and shallowest, making flow diversion the most economical, based on the survey and on-site investigations. Dejiong personally inspected and verified that this location was indeed suitable and decided to divert the flow there. A light railway will immediately be laid from the Bato of the Si Gong dam to prevent the water level from rising and overflowing from both ends during the flow diversion. One end of the water barrier dam has already been built, and most of the materials have been transported. The flow diversion work is scheduled to begin on the 20th of this month. The flow diversion method has been studied in detail by the Bureau, taking into account the sediment content, velocity, terrain, and other conditions of the water flow at that location, and it has been decided that the closure can be completed before February 10th. The amount of earthwork for the Yaodi is very large, and whether it can be completed before the flood season depends on the number of workers. Although the county governments have been requested to recommend contractors to the project office, the contractors initially delayed signing contracts, intending to demand an increase in the unit price. After repeated persuasion by the project office, and changing the wage distribution from actual wages to 90% of actual wages, they gradually signed contracts. The agreed unit price, the specified deadline, and the number of workers to be provided are all stated in the contract. However, after signing, the contractors still did not bring all the workers to the site, in order to coerce and threaten. Subsequently, after discussions between the Department of Public Works and representatives from the Sixth District Administrative Inspectorate Commissioner's Office, a subsidy of 1.2 jiao per square yard was added to the unit price of 5 jiao for rain work, bringing the total unit price to a minimum of 6.2 jiao and a maximum of 9.2 jiao. The average price, including ramming work, reached the maximum amount of 8.5 jiao of the approved budget. The representative of the Commissioner's Office signed the agreement, requiring the workers to arrive in full force by the 20th of this month. Although there has been a slight increase in enthusiasm, the number of workers who have arrived is still less than 10,000. Under these circumstances, the Bureau is deeply concerned that it will still be difficult to avoid them attempting to coerce and threaten by slowing down work or withdrawing workers in the future. It is requested that the importance and urgency of the project be considered, and that the Sixth District Administrative Inspectorate Commissioner's Office be instructed to strictly urge the county governments to urge the contractors to supervise the workers and order them to arrive in full force. If there are any more cases of slowing down work or desertion, administrative force should be used to supervise them. If the contractors are fearful, they will not dare to arbitrarily coerce and threaten again, so that the work can be completed as soon as possible. Director of the Bureau, Xi Dejiong, is scheduled to personally supervise the work at the project site in the coming days. However, if it becomes necessary to leave the project site, Chief Engineer Lin Youlong will act on his behalf. (January 15th)

Journey to Nanchang (Part 1) - The Opening Ceremony of the Yushan-Nanchang Section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway and Other Matters - 74

In recent years, our country's government authorities have spared no effort in the construction of aviation and highways. East-west transportation south of the Yangtze River has always relied on ports, rivers, and lakes as shortcuts. Now, a significant transformation has begun. The substantial completion of highway networks among the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan serves as a concrete illustration. As a result, inland transportation has become greatly facilitated. However, in terms of safety, comfort, accuracy, speed, freedom, and low costs, highway transportation still lags far behind railway transportation. The urgent desire for railway expansion is therefore more pressing. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, a crucial inland transportation artery between the Yangtze River and Pearl River basins, has managed to complete a portion of its construction with economical financial resources, a short timeframe, and under the management of domestic technical personnel.

Construction Planning of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway

The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway was originally planned to start from Hangzhou in Zhejiang and end at Pingxiang in Jiangxi, with a total length of 904 kilometers. Among them, the section from Hangzhou via Xiaoshan, Zhuji, Yiwu, Jinhua, Tangxi, Longyou, Quzhou, and Jiangshan to Yushan in Jiangxi, totaling 341 kilometers, was originally named the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. Construction began in March of the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930) and was completed and opened to traffic in December of the 22nd year (1933). The 292-kilometer section from Yushan via Shangrao, Hengfeng, Yiyang, Guixi, Dongxiang, and Jinxian to Nanchang – called the Yushan-Nanchang Section – began preparations immediately after the opening of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. In April of the 23rd year (1934), construction was approved by the Ministry of Railways and the Zhejiang and Jiangxi provincial governments. As for the 263-kilometer section between Nanchang and Pingxiang – the Nanchang-Pingxiang Section – construction also commenced on the day of the opening ceremony of the Yushan-Nanchang Section on the 15th of this month.

The construction capital for this section was funded by the issuance of public bonds of 12 million yuan each by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Finance, totaling 24 million yuan. Using the bond face value and all assets after the completion of the Yushan-Nanchang Section as collateral, loans and advances were borrowed from the Shanghai banking group and the German company Otto Wolff for purchasing materials, amounting to 16 million yuan. A joint venture called the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway United Company was established to oversee all aspects of the entire railway. Starting from July 20th of the 23rd year (1934), the entire section was divided into four general sections and sixteen sub-sections, and construction commenced simultaneously. It took 17 months to complete the construction by December of the 24th year (1935). If there had been no disruptions caused by floods and bandits during this period, it could have been opened to traffic as early as last year's National Day.

Inviting Guests from All Walks of Life

After the reporter received the invitation from the Board of Directors of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway United Company for the opening ceremony of the Yushan-Nanchang Section to be held in Nanchang on the 15th of this month, he and a group of eighteen reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers in Shanghai took the Beijing-Zhabei express train to Hangzhou at 3 PM on the 13th. According to the invitation, they were to arrive at the Sanlangmiao waiting area at the Nanxing Bridge Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway before 8 PM that evening.

As the train passed Jiaxing, light snow began to fall. Although Yuanhu Lake was at its lowest water level, it and the Misty Rain Pavilion in the lake seemed to be covered with a layer of white gauze, presenting a unique and exquisite charm. The train arrived at Nanwu Bridge, and darkness fell, the clouds already deep.

The reception for the opening ceremony had already dispatched several staff members to the station to greet the guests. (Originally, their invitation was not limited to Shanghai newspaper reporters, but also included those from Nanjing and Hangzhou, and most importantly, the Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Huang Shaohong, and the Vice Minister of Railways, Zeng Yangfu – who also served as Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway United Company, so he could be considered the host – Legislative Member Ma Yinchu, and other important political figures, members of the financial and industrial sectors, and local officials along the railway.) In total, there were over three hundred people. They had prepared more than ten small chartered cars and buses to transport the guests to the Sanlangmiao pier, which was the main ferry crossing before the completion of the Qiantang River Bridge. Every day, from 6 AM to 6 PM, there was a constant stream of passengers traveling between the two banks of the Qiantang River, being transported by the Qiantang River Ferry. A new-style steel-reinforced concrete pier had been built at the riverbank, extending from the shallow beach to the floating dock in the center of the river, about half a li in length. This was wide enough for two cars to pass each other.

Crossing the Qiantang River on a Snowy Night

When the reporter arrived there, it was about 8 o'clock. Although there was no particularly biting cold wind on the river, the snow was falling even more heavily. At the floating dock, the enthusiastic reception staff was waiting, issuing numbered sleeper tickets for the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway according to the invitation numbers. By the time we got off the ferry, our hands and feet were already numb with cold. The ferry was a large wooden boat with high-raised ends, with a cabin that could accommodate twenty people. Perhaps it was special that evening, but there was a bright kerosene lamp hanging inside. On the dimly lit river, every two ferries were towed across the river by a small steamboat.

The Xixing riverside pier also had such a new-style pier and floating dock. However, the pier was open-air. There were already many cars waiting to welcome the guests and take them to the station. In fact, if viewed in daylight, the distance between the pier and the station might be only a stone's throw away.

A Glimpse of the Special Train's Arrangement

The Hangzhou-Jiangshan section uses 35-pound light rails, so the locomotives and passenger cars are also limited. The car bodies are shorter and lower compared to those on the Beijing-Shanghai line, and perhaps even narrower (although the distance between the two rails is the same as on the Beijing-Shanghai line). However, the equipment inside the cars is relatively complete. The special train parked at the riverside station consisted of fifteen cars, including first, second, and third-class seating and sleeping cars. The dignitaries were traveling in an "office car" with complete bedding. The Party and national flags were crossed at the front of the car, covered with paper flowers. Inside the carriages, there were also many colorful paper flowers and ribbons hanging beautifully.

The catering for all three hundred guests on the train was contracted to Tianxianglou, the largest restaurant in Hangzhou. The owner was also dressed as a waiter, taking care of the arrangements in the car. Each guest paid 6 jiao per meal. Each table of four had four dishes and a hot pot. The reception stipulated that he must use local products from along the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway as raw materials. At 9 PM on the 13th, everyone enjoyed the dinner very much. At 10 PM, the train departed, and the guests gradually entered the sleeping cars to sleep.

Each sleeping car had two attendants managing the berths, doors, windows, and toilets. Seeing how politely they accepted the passengers' requests, it was clear that they had received considerable training. All thirty of them served on this special train, with eighteen assigned to each. Most of them spoke with a Zhejiang accent, and their ages ranged from sixteen to twenty-five. They wore yellow woolen uniforms, and their hats also had "flying wheel" emblems. They were in good spirits and physical condition. Their monthly salary ranged from ten to fifteen yuan, and they were not allowed to accept tips from passengers. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Company also did not abandon its obligation to continue educating them. They have now established employee children's schools in Jiangbian, Jinhua, Yushan, and other places, giving them the opportunity to receive education.

The Train Passes Jiangshan at Dawn

The train traveled steadily, and the sound of the wheels accompanied many large and small stations and beautiful scenery throughout the night. On the morning of January 14th, the weather was gloomy. The train stopped at Jiangshan Station. Peering out the window from the sleeper berth, the distant mountains were still so green, but nearby, one could only see rolling red and yellow earthen hills. Small houses were scattered in the mountainous area. Three or five village children were still staring blankly at the train, which they had already seen many times. Material civilization has not yet fully penetrated this ancient land – even in the culturally rich region of Zhejiang and Jiangsu.

After passing Jiangshan, the scenery completely lost the elegant charm of the area near Hangzhou. From here until Yushan, west of the Jiangxi provincial border, was the area where the Red Bandits roamed a year ago. On each hilltop and strategic pass, one could see the blockhouses that prevented the Red Bandits from gaining a foothold in Jiangxi. Now that this area has been cleared, these blockhouses have become merely decorations in these desolate mountains.

Scenery Along the Yushan-Nanchang Line

At 9:30 AM, we arrived at Yushan, which was the original terminus of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. Further ahead was Yushan, the starting point of the Yushan-Nanchang section. Yushan Station occupies a large area and has many branch lines. In the future, it will definitely become the largest distribution station for goods in the upper reaches of the Xin River. When the train entered the station, the station staff set off many firecrackers. They also built a decorated archway on the railway west of the station, allowing the first train to pass underneath and onto the newly completed Yushan-Nanchang section.

Around 11 AM, we arrived at Shangrao. This place had been occupied by the Red Bandits three times, and the local area suffered great losses. The population had drastically decreased from 300,000 to 240,000. The main products are tea, paper, and ramie cloth. In the past, annual sales of each item reached 500,000 yuan, but now things are not what they used to be. Shangrao and its surrounding counties of Yushan, Guangfeng, Qianshan, Yiyang, and Hengfeng each have 300 blockhouses within their borders, totaling nearly 2,000 in the six counties. In this area, one often doesn't see any signs of human habitation for dozens of li. Even if there are, one only sees a few dilapidated mud houses, some without windows, and the walls still bearing the large-character slogans written by the Red Bandits back then. Last year, the Yushan-Nanchang section project encountered great obstacles here. First, it encountered unprecedented heavy rainfall, which affected the work. Second, there were still many Red Bandits scattered in this area, who often invaded the lodgings of the road workers, killing refugees who had escaped from the Red areas and were considered by them to be reactionaries, and coercing recruited road workers to go to the Red areas. In addition, "after the war, there is always a famine," and there was also a severe epidemic of malaria. As a result, no less than 2,000 road workers sacrificed their lives in this section.

Twenty-three kilometers west of Shangrao, along the railway, there is a coal mine called Kengkour. Although the coal seams in the mine are mostly poor, the upper layer of the Dachong Mine contains excellent coal that can be used for locomotive fuel and ordinary furnaces and blacksmithing. It is worth mining. The length of the coal seams, according to current estimates, is 2,700 meters, the thickness of the coal seams is 3 meters, and the minable depth is 719 meters. The amount of coal that can be mined is 5,299,749 tons. If 300 tons are produced per day, it can last for 50 years. The railway has plans to mine it to supply its own needs.

After passing Hengfeng and Yiyang, we arrived at Guixi. Twenty-five kilometers south of the station is Longhu Mountain, the so-called birthplace of Taoism. The former residence of the Taoist patriarch Zhang Daoling is located there. Near Guixi, there is also a large bridge, second only to the large bridge near Liangjiadu in the railway's bridge engineering projects. It has thirteen arches and is 390 meters long, costing nearly 500,000 yuan.

Arriving in Nanchang Late at Night

After this, darkness fell again. But at each station, people set off firecrackers to welcome us, and there were always soldiers and police on guard near the station. It wasn't until 10 PM that the lights of Nanchang could be seen outside the train window. The reception had already contacted Nanchang by long-distance telephone from the previous two stations, arranging for all the guests to stay at major hotels.

The long train journey of nearly thirty hours finally came to an end at 10:30 PM. Amidst the symphony of military music and firecrackers, the train entered Nanchang Station. Over two hundred people, including the Chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, Xiong Shihui, important figures from various political parties, Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway personnel, and local newspaper reporters, gathered on the platform to welcome us. Huang Shaohong and Zeng Yangfu were the first to get off the train, receiving salutes from the local army, which presented a grand military appearance.

After exiting the station, we boarded highway buses and were taken to designated hotels. Everyone was exhausted and fell asleep as soon as they lay down. On the afternoon of January 14th, the reporter interviewed the Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Huang Shaohong, and the Vice Minister of Railways, Zeng Yangfu, in the train. According to Huang, regarding local administration in Zhejiang, he intends to increase the power of the county governments, and is currently in the testing phase. The reason why we can't start in all counties simultaneously is just like a parent with children: those who can be independent are allowed to be independent, but those who cannot be independent still need parental supervision. Continuing to talk about the current situation, Huang said that the issues of the 29th Army and North China can be used as an example. Just as the demise of the Southern Song Dynasty was blamed by later generations on Qin Hui's advocacy of peace, Yue Fei's advocacy of war would not necessarily have defeated the Jin army. Moreover, the Southern Song Dynasty was destroyed a hundred years after Qin Hui's death. The responsibility lies not with Qin Hui and Emperor Gaozong, but with the foolish monarchs after Gaozong. The North China issue can also be viewed in a similar way. The Southwest has no intention of destroying the country. If national affairs can be considered from a broad and long-term perspective, no problem is unsolvable. Political problems can be easily solved if the environment is favorable. Regarding the Mongolian issue, he said that Prince Yun is old and weak, and his mind is muddled, so he is not capable of doing anything. However, Prince De has great ambitions, so the Mongolian issue is very complex.

According to Zeng Yangfu, "The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway starts from Hangzhou and extends to Yushan, then to Nanchang, and connects to the Zhuzhou-Pingxiang Railway at Pingxiang, linking to the Guangdong-Hankou Railway. To the east, it can reach Shanghai, and to the south, it can go directly to Guangzhou. Therefore, the commencement of the Nanchang-Pingxiang section and the opening of the Yushan-Nanchang section will be held on the same day. The construction cost of the Nanchang-Pingxiang section is 18 million yuan, similar to the Yushan-Nanchang section. We borrowed 10 million yuan from the Shanghai banking group and 8 million yuan from the German Otto Wolff Company. A preliminary agreement was signed in April last year, so there should be no problem with securing the loan. The Yushan-Nanchang section, which has now been completed, uses 65-pound heavy rails throughout, except for the Hangzhou-Yushan section, which uses 35-pound light rails. We hope to achieve a permanent solution. However, due to the weight of the rails, the vehicles on the Hangzhou-Yushan section can travel to Nanchang, but the vehicles on the Yushan-Nanchang section cannot enter the Hangzhou-Yushan section. It is planned to replace the light rails on the Hangzhou-Yushan section with heavy rails within this year. By next year, after the completion of the Qiantang River Railway Bridge, the Nanchang-Pingxiang section, and the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, all railways in the country can be directly connected. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway also plans to use diesel locomotives to shorten travel time, so that it can depart from Hangzhou at 7 AM and arrive in Nanchang at 5 PM on the same day. Currently, the roadbed is not yet solid, and everything is still in the initial stages. At the same time, there is no current need for this. For the safety of the journey, the train is running relatively slowly."

Songjiang: Convicts in Robbery Case Sentenced to Imprisonment 75

The case of the robbery of a joint transport vehicle in the Yanggongmiao area of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway has been repeatedly ordered by the provincial government to be investigated and brought to justice, and measures have been properly planned to protect the safety of vehicles. Later, the county government strictly ordered its subordinates to arrest the perpetrators. The water patrol team searched and arrested the two main robbery criminals, Zhang Xiaobao and He Xiaohashang, in Caojing Shuike. They confessed that the ringleader, Li Jinxiang, had escaped without a trace. They pleaded guilty to the facts of the robbery. The county sent them to the local court for trial. After repeated interrogations, Xiaobaogen was sentenced to eighteen years of imprisonment and He Xiaohashang to fourteen years of imprisonment today (the 18th) as a warning.

Wuxi: Silk Market Soars, Silk Factories Revive 76

In December of last year, Wuxi's silk factories were forced to shut down due to sluggish sales in Europe, with prices falling from over 800 yuan per dan to around 700 yuan, coupled with a severe shortage of raw materials. However, recently, the silk market has seen a unanimous rise in prices both domestically and internationally. This is due to the disruption of silk sources and the limited production of Japanese silk. American silk factories, aware that new silk will not be available for several months and that the spring sales season is approaching, are eager to purchase large quantities. As a result, they are actively buying, and in the past two weeks, the price of Chinese silk has gradually soared. High-grade white factory silk has risen to around 850 yuan per package, and user silk is also at 720-730 yuan. Only a few factories in Wuxi, such as Huaxin, Yongtai, and Qianxin, as well as ten factories including Yongsheng, Dasheng, Minfeng, Jinji, and Yuqi, are still operating as usual. They plan to stop work for a week at the end of the old lunar year. As for the other factories, Yongli Company, newly established by Xue Shoucha, Wang Huanan, Zheng Bingquan, and others, has leased 37 of them and plans to start production in full after the new cocoons come onto the market.

County Chamber of Commerce Re-election Completed 77

The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce held its third re-election of half of its members on the 10th of this month. The seven elected executive committee members were Jiang Daoshan, Yang Weizhang, Jiang Jinghai, Xue Shouxuan, Miao Suchen, Tang Xinghai, and Xue Huidong. The three elected supervisory committee members were Yang Hanxi, Cai Xiesan, and Xue Songliang. Yesterday (the 18th) afternoon, the first joint meeting of the new and old executive and supervisory committees was held, and the organization was reorganized. Qian Sunqing, Cheng Jingtang, Chen Zhanru, Wu Shimei, and Xue Shouxuan were elected as standing committee members, with Qian Sunqing as the chairman of the standing committee.

General Re-census of the Entire County 78

The county government convened its 65th district chiefs' meeting yesterday, chaired by County Magistrate Long. It was decided to conduct a general re-census of the entire county from January 27th to 29th. The "Implementation Measures for the General Re-census" and "Precautions for District Chiefs" were also approved. Each district chief should convene a meeting of township and village heads to take responsibility for the general re-census. The county has collected considerable revenue from sales deeds and contract taxes, and it was decided to thoroughly rectify the tax collection to increase revenue. The meeting was adjourned after discussions.

Changzhou: Murder and Body Disposal Case in the Third District 79

Tan Guangyu, the Jia head of the sixth Jia of the third Bao of the Nanyin Township in the third district of Wujin, was tasked with patrolling the watch post. On the evening of the 13th of this month, he led the post guards Tan Falong and Tan Faming on patrol in the vicinity. To their surprise, Tan Guangyu did not return home by dawn. His wife, Zhou, searched everywhere but could not find him. Tan Falong and Tan Faming were also missing. Realizing that something must be amiss, she ordered the post guards to investigate. Bloodstains were found all over Tan Falong's house, indicating that Falong had been murdered. It was learned that Falong had fled to the Qingcheng area. Tan Zhou immediately asked the township Bao head to report to the Third Sub-station of the Public Security Bureau and request police assistance. They arrested Tan Falong, Tan Faming, and Tan Jiangshi in Qingcheng. After a preliminary interrogation, they all confessed to murdering Tan Guangyu. They confessed that they first struck Guangyu's head with a gong hammer, then strangled his neck with a coarse hemp rope, and then took a kitchen knife and slashed his head twice, killing him instantly. In order to cover up the crime, they carried the body to the river and dumped it into the river. Inspector Deng Zuyu immediately sent people to try to retrieve the body. It was found on the riverbank. On the 16th, he prepared a document to report to the Procuratorate of the Local Court and requested that personnel be dispatched for an examination. It was heard that Prosecutor Guan Junjie had been appointed and led his staff to the countryside on the morning of the 17th to examine the body. The criminals have been sent to the city for trial.

Water Transportation Interrupted 80

Since the beginning of winter, this area has experienced rain and snow, but the climate has remained mild as in autumn. However, after the 16th of this month, the northwest wind roared, and the weather changed dramatically, turning extremely cold. As a result, the indoor temperature on the Fahrenheit scale has plummeted to 26 degrees below freezing in the past two days. As a result, water freezes into ice, and bathhouses and bathhouses are thriving. However, rivers, harbors, ponds, and pools are all frozen, and small steamships and sailing ships traveling to and from the city and countryside have been interrupted. Although water transport to other ports has been cut off, it has had no impact since the introduction of automobiles last autumn.

Changshu: Elderly Man Run Over and Killed on Highway 81

The seventh car of the Xihu Automobile Company, traveling to Wuxi yesterday, was passing the Twenty-Nine Bridge area near Liantang when an elderly man suddenly came into view. He was deaf and blind and could not avoid the car to the left or right. The driver, Yang Lie, could not avoid him in time, and the old man from the township was knocked over and his head hit the back of the car. The car immediately transported the injured old man back to Changshu and sent him to the hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he died shortly after. The driver, on orders from the station, surrendered to the Public Security Bureau. It was later learned that the deceased old man was named Ding Guanda, aged sixteen. After being transferred to the County Justice Department, he was ordered to reach a settlement with the family, paying funeral expenses and compensation.

Jiangyin: Yangku Sailing Ship Robbed 82

At about 2 AM on the 16th, a sailing ship traveling from Yangku to the city arrived near Jintong Bridge, when it was suddenly encountered by more than ten bandits. They shouted for the ship to stop along the river, and each of them, carrying guns and weapons, boarded the ship and searched it arbitrarily. It was estimated that they robbed 470 yuan in legal tender from Deda and other businesses, and 60 yuan from the passengers. After the shipowner, Xie Chunlin, arrived in the city, he reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau and requested that the county investigate. County Magistrate Yan, upon receiving the report, ordered the security team to strengthen patrols, as theft cases have occurred frequently in the four townships during this winter prevention period.

The Provincial Order on the Exchange of Buildings between the Public Security Bureau and the District Office Requires Proper Planning 83

The Public Security Bureau does not have enough buildings and will exchange them with the First District Office. Local people have opposed this exchange because they believe that county property should not be entangled with local public property. After the political affairs meeting, it was decided to submit a request to the Department of Civil Affairs for instructions. The instructions stated that since local objections have arisen, the original proposers should be ordered to discuss proper solutions again.

Nantong: Tax Police Fight in Rugao 84

Zhuo Cha and Liu Junying, Wu Jugui and other officers of the Ninth District Tax Police stationed in Rugao, were watching a play at the Tianhou Palace in Rugao. Because they were fighting for seats, there was a conflict with Lu Kaisheng, the County Trial Officer. Lu's head was broken, and his attendant was arrested. This case was classified as judicial and was transferred to the jurisdiction of the Higher Court. The Nantong Local Court heard the case. On the 17th, the criminal court concluded the trial and sentenced Zhuo Cha and others to five months' imprisonment each.

General Re-census of the Entire County 85

Nantong County is scheduled to hold a general re-census from February 1st to 3rd. District, township, village, and Bao heads are all mobilized. Beforehand, Bao and Jia training meetings will be held to promote the census at each level in order to ensure its smooth implementation.

Yangzhou: Military Review Committee Arrives in Yangzhou 86

Yan Ming, the Training Commissioner of the Fifth Security District of Jiangsu Province, was ordered to assemble the security teams stationed in the counties of Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Xinghua, and Dongtai under his jurisdiction in Yangzhou to await inspection by personnel dispatched by the Military Affairs Commission. They have successively departed for Yangzhou. It is learned that the review committee dispatched by the Military Affairs Commission is led by Lieutenant General Yang Jingzhi, the director, and includes committee members Chang Hefeng, Shao Bi, the director of the sub-section, and more than ten others. They arrived in Shaobo from Huainan on the evening of the 16th. However, due to the cold weather and frozen river, the ship could not travel. After receiving the news, Commissioner Yan still supervised the team to go to Shaobo by land to welcome and protect them. The county government also sent Squad Leader Jiang, leading the box-gun squad, to welcome them into the city and arranged for them to stay at the Dalu Hotel on Xin Sheng Street in Jiangbei. A review will be held at the Zhunti Temple exercise ground in the city at 9 AM on the 18th.

Xing Fang Reappointed as Anti-Smoking Instructor 87

Instructor Xing Fang, who was previously in Yangzhou to conduct the household registration survey, has been recognized by the province for his excellent results and for his exceptional familiarity with the situation in the county. Therefore, he has recently been appointed as the Anti-Smoking Instructor of Jiangdu. He arrived in Yangzhou on the 16th and, on the afternoon of the 17th, gathered the First District Chief Wang Zhu and the township and village heads and township officers under his jurisdiction, as well as the patrol officers from each Public Security Sub-station, at the Public Education Center to discuss the self-renewal registration of smokers and the methods for the general denunciation. Lu Dajun, the chief of the Anti-Smoking Section of the county government, participated. A total of more than 200 people attended. First, Chief Lu gave a detailed account of the process of self-renewal registration, and then Instructor Xing gave a speech, providing guidance on the points to be noted in the self-renewal registration and general denunciation. Any concealment or failure to report should be severely punished according to the law. The meeting adjourned at noon. It was also learned that Instructor Xing, accompanied by Chief Lu, is scheduled to go to Guazhou on the morning of the 18th to convene a meeting of the self-governing public security personnel of the Second District, and then go to other townships to investigate and ban smoking from house to house, in order to ensure that the prohibition of drugs is thorough and that no one is left out.

Weather Turns Cold, Canal Freezes 88

Since the beginning of winter, Yangzhou City has experienced two snowfalls, but the river water has not frozen. However, last night (the 16th), the wind roared, and although today (the 17th) is sunny, the water in basins and other containers has all frozen solid. The ferry on Yangqing Road, heading to Shaobo, had to return midway due to the frozen river. Yang Jinwen, the Lieutenant General of the inspection team sent by the Military Affairs Commission to review the security teams of seven counties including Jiangdu, was still in Shaobo due to the river being frozen. All the administrative personnel were staying at the Dalu Hotel on Xin Sheng Street in Yangzhou, waiting quietly.

Shaoxing Shaoxing District Training for Baozhang (Neighborhood Chiefs) Method 89

He Yangling, the Administrative Inspector of Shaoxing District, received an order to draft a method for training Baozhang. It was found that the quota for Baozhang in each county was as follows: Shaoxing 2309, Yuyao 1427, Shangyu 728, Xiaoshan 1014, Zhuji 1214, Xinchang 624, Shengxian 1030, totaling 8346. Due to the large number of people, it was specially proposed to conduct training in four locations: one specifically in Shaoxing, one jointly in Yuyao and Shangyu with the location in Yuyao, one jointly in Xiaoshan and Zhuji with the location in Zhuji, and one jointly in Shengxian and Xinchang with the location in Shengxian. Each location would be divided into three training sessions, each lasting two months. The total cost for the four locations would be 200,000 yuan. A telegram was sent to the provincial government yesterday for approval, instructing that the training period for each session should still follow the regulations and last for three months. The required funds are severely insufficient, and it was instructed to make practical cuts and use the most economical method for proper allocation.

Hangzhou The Municipal Government Takes Over the Provincial County Guidance Bureau 90

The Zhejiang Provincial County Guidance Bureau received an order from the Construction Department to handle the closing, and the provincial government meeting decided that it would be taken over by the Hangzhou Municipal Government concurrently to save expenses. It is now known that the Municipal Government received the order from the provincial government starting today (18th), and has assigned personnel to prepare for the takeover procedures. They have also contacted the responsible personnel of the Bureau and plan to merge with the Municipal Government next week. The Bureau's address will be relocated to the Xunwen Office on the Baidi embankment at Broken Bridge in West Lake.

Pinghu A Large Number of Anhui Refugees Cause Trouble 91

On the 14th of this month, suddenly more than one hundred Anhui refugees gathered at the Hongni Weir in Zhapu, forcibly demanding grain and rice from the local residents. The township office sent people to suppress them, but they were resisted. As a last resort, more than ten shots were fired as a warning. The refugees, upon hearing the shots, gathered and seized Zhao Yangyun, a clerk from the township office, snatched his gun, and stole one yuan and three jiao from his person. The county Public Security Section received the report and immediately dispatched several patrol officers with arms to drive them away. Currently, the refugees have left Zhapu City and have now arrived in Beihe Jian Township, not far from the city.

A Guest Disappears from the Jiu Feng Inn 92

A few days ago, a man named Yang from Sichuan stayed at the Jiu Feng Inn in Zhapu. Later, he sought help from his uncle to find a job, but was instead scolded and rebuked. Overwhelmed with resentment and anger, he said he wanted to commit suicide. Other guests tried their best to persuade him, and he finally went to bed reluctantly. Yesterday, this guest suddenly disappeared without a trace. He was nowhere to be found, and he did not take any of his luggage. It is feared that something unfortunate has happened to him.

Local News

North China Customs, Salt Taxes and Road Funds Are Still Being Submitted to the Central Government as Usual 93

Reuter's, Shanghai, January 18 - Reuter's learns from reliable sources that the rumors that North China Customs, salt taxes, and railway revenues have been withheld by the North China authorities are incorrect. The various taxes are currently being submitted to the Central Government as usual.

Salt Tax Revenue Increases in 1935 94

According to the preliminary statistics of the Salt Revenue Audit Office for 1935, the total salt tax revenue was 184,209,300 national currency, an increase of 8,259,300 yuan compared to the 175,950,000 yuan collected in 1934. Last year, financial conditions were tight, commerce was depressed, and there was a severe flood in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, which greatly affected salt transportation. Despite this, the tax revenue was still able to achieve this result, which is truly remarkable. The tax revenue of each region is listed below in order of magnitude. However, these figures are based on preliminary reports from various locations, and may be subject to revision after a detailed audit of the accounts. Changlu (including the Koubei area) - 26,775,200 national currency, Huaibei - 19,555,300 yuan, Sichuan (including the Chongqing area) - 15,620,900 yuan, E'an - 14,652,200 yuan, Xiang'an - 13,387,400 yuan, Yangzhou - 13,356,100 yuan, Songjiang - 12,568,000 yuan, Youdong - 9,672,800 yuan, Guangdong - 9,290,500 yuan, Xi'an - 9,085,300 yuan, Liangzhe - 9,006,700 yuan, Henan - 7,703,200 yuan, Wan'an - 6,083,600 yuan, Fujian - 4,715,600 yuan, Hedong - 4,067,100 yuan, Yunnan - 2,095,800 yuan, Chuanbei - 2,092,700 yuan, Shaanxi - 1,479,700 yuan, General Office - 1,206,300 yuan, Jinbei - 1,004,900 yuan, Total - 184,209,300 national currency.

Silver Prices Decline, Exchange Rate Stabilizes, Balance Tax Temporarily Suspended, Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee Held a Meeting Yesterday Morning 95

It is still difficult to predict whether we will recover in the future. The Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee of the Central Bank, due to the low price of silver abroad and the disappearance of silver exports, has stabilized the exchange rate and temporarily suspended the balance tax yesterday. Whether or not it will be restored in the future depends on the situation. The details are recorded as follows:

Temporary Suspension of Balance Tax: Members of the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee of the Central Bank: Xi Demao of the Central Bank, Bei Songsun of the Bank of China, and Zhang Peishen of the Bank of Communications, met again at the Business Bureau of the Central Bank at 10:00 AM yesterday morning to discuss the balance tax rate. It was agreed that there was no need for a balance tax at the moment due to the low price of silver abroad and the balanced exchange rates of various countries. It was decided to temporarily suspend the announcement for one day yesterday. The balance tax was immediately announced to be 0.00%, a new record since its implementation. According to a New News Agency reporter who inquired with the committee, although the balance tax was not announced yesterday, this is a temporary measure. Whether it will continue to be suspended in the future or announced as usual is still unpredictable and depends on the decision of the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee.

Stable Foreign Exchange: The Central Bank announced the selling price of telegraphic transfers yesterday morning, converted as follows: London - 1 shilling, 2 and a half pence per national currency yuan; New York - 29.75 US dollars; Paris - 452 francs; Berlin - 73.75 marks; Japan - 103 yen; Hong Kong - 93 Hong Kong dollars (all above are per 100 national currency yuan). The exchange rates listed by HSBC were the same as the Central Bank's. The above exchange rates for each country are standard prices, and the foreign exchange departments of various banks settle accounts according to the prices listed by the Central Bank. Therefore, the foreign exchange rate is considered stable.

Qian Industry Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday, Announcing the Overall Closing Method 96

An announcement was issued yesterday: The period for the overall closing of various industries in 1935 is approaching. The Qian Industry Association not only sent letters to its members, the money houses, but also announced in the market: "To whom it may concern, the proposal regarding the handling of business before and after the overall closing, proposed at the third regular meeting of the third session of member representatives, has been approved. The resolution is listed below. The overall closing period for 1935 has been set (resolution) for January 23rd. According to regulations, there will be a four-day holiday from the 24th to the 27th to organize everything, and this four-day period will be for the dismissal period. Resolution on the interest issue before the overall closing: 2.5 yuan. Resolution on the ticket collection period: ticket collection will start from January 19th and end at 4:00 PM, and ticket returns will be extended by one hour as usual. Tickets will be cleared as they arrive on the 23rd. Resolution on interbank interest rates: interbank interest rates will be open until January 22nd. The above resolutions are recorded on file and are hereby recorded for your information. Please investigate and handle accordingly. This is for the attention of all member money houses."

Heavy Collection and Clearance: The Qian Industry Association held a regular meeting of the executive committee at 2:00 PM yesterday. Executive committee members such as Lu Shuchen and Liu Wuqiao attended and discussed matters concerning the overall closing for 1935 before adjourning. Starting today, the time for ticket collection at various money houses will be extended to 4:00 PM, and the time for ticket returns will be extended by one hour as usual. The interbank interest rate in the market was still 8 fen per 1,000 yuan per day in both the morning and afternoon sessions yesterday. However, the collection and clearance of both the silver and money industries were particularly heavy. The total amount of exchange at the bank bill clearing house was 19,561,060 yuan, 0 jiao, and 7 fen, of which the collection on behalf of the Qian Industry has increased to 3,413,695 yuan, 6 jiao, and 5 fen.

Summoned by Beijing for Inquiry, Yu and Others Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning, No Comment on Rumors of Reduced Interest Rates and Postponement of Public Bonds 97

The atmosphere in the exchange is still strong, and securities have fallen sharply. Yu Zuoting, chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, standing committee member Jin Runxiang, member of the National Debt Fund Custody Committee Wang Xiaolai, and secretary Kang Hou, were summoned by telegram by the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance. After going to Beijing the day before yesterday, they returned to Shanghai on the Beijing-Shanghai night express train at 11:00 PM that night. The train was originally scheduled to arrive at Shanghai North Station at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, but due to the cold weather, the train was delayed by 25 minutes and arrived at 7:25 AM. A reporter from the New Voice News met Yu, Jin, Wang, and Lin at the North Station. According to them, after arriving in Beijing, the Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, Weng Wenhao, and the Deputy Chairman of the Executive Yuan presented three reasons why it was impossible to reduce interest rates and postpone public bonds. Minister Kong and others attached great importance to this matter. The reporter also asked if the reduction of interest rates and postponement of public bonds was due to a misunderstanding, but the four of them made no comment.

December Coupon Interest: The National Debt Fund Management Committee paid the following in December of last year: 342,307 yuan and 5 jiao and 3 fen in interest for the 18th year customs tax bonds, 464,100 yuan in interest for the compiled bonds, 811,200 yuan in interest for the 19th year customs tax bonds, 492,600 yuan in interest for the 19th year rehabilitation bonds, 528,060 yuan in interest for the 20th year tobacco bonds, 606,400 yuan in interest for the 20th year customs tax bonds, 736,640 yuan in interest for the 20th year consolidated tax bonds, 744,960 yuan in interest for the 20th year salt tax bonds, 500,000 yuan in interest for patriotic bonds, 935,000 yuan in interest for the 22nd year customs tax bonds, 692,500 yuan in interest for the 23rd year customs tax bonds, 550,000 yuan in interest for the 24th year Sichuan financial consolidation bonds, 669,000 yuan in interest for the 20th year disaster relief bonds, 489,530 yuan, 0 jiao, and 0.05 fen in interest for the consolidated 6% bonds, 122,400 yuan in interest for the consolidated 7% bonds, 960,000 yuan in interest for the Yuping Railway bonds, 753,750 yuan in interest for the 7th year 6% bonds, 1,218,000 yuan in interest for the 14th year bonds, 272,160 yuan in interest for the military bonds, 824,000 yuan in interest for the rehabilitation short-term bonds, 282,500 yuan in interest for the 18th year disaster relief bonds, 390,075 yuan in interest for the 19th year customs tax bonds, 30,000 yuan in interest for the security bonds, 2,485,000 yuan in interest for the 23rd year customs tax bonds, 450,000 yuan in interest for the 23rd year telecommunications bonds, and 70,680 yuan in interest for the Austrian indemnity 25 bonds, totaling 14,179,932 yuan, 5 jiao, and 3 fen.

Rumors Unabated in the Trading Market, All Securities Plunge: Since the securities market of the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange was filled with rumors of reduced interest rates and postponement of public bonds, the prices of various public bonds and bonds have plummeted across the board. After the market opened yesterday morning, the Ministry of Finance responded to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's telegram requesting protection of public bond credit, stating that the government would resolutely consolidate debt credit and hoped to earnestly convey this message to merchants and people, urging them not to be exploited by speculators and to avoid self-inflicted panic. However, the rumors of reduced interest rates and postponement of bonds in the market have not subsided, resulting in a continued plunge in the prices of various public bonds and bonds. As a result, the demobilization bonds and the 19th year rehabilitation bonds fell to 4 yuan and trading was suspended. The remaining 20th year consolidated tax, financial, and short-term bonds all fell by several jiao to 2-3 yuan. Trading was very heavy, and brokers requested that each session be reduced by one round in both the morning and afternoon.

Ministry of Finance to Establish Large-Scale Storage Warehouses in Datun 98

Seeking National Food Self-Sufficiency: The National Economic Council, in view of the frequent floods and droughts in recent years, the emptiness of food reserves, and the opportunistic imports of foreign rice, resulting in a trade deficit of as much as 70 million yuan, believes that China, as a rice-producing country, is instead being flooded by foreign rice. If measures are not taken to strive for self-sufficiency, the future will be even more unthinkable. Therefore, it specially consulted with the Executive Yuan's Rural Reconstruction Committee and relevant ministries, and it was decided to establish a General Administration of Food in Shanghai to control the scattered and unfounded imports of foreign rice that disrupt the market, and to plan to establish a large-scale national grain storage warehouse in Jiujiang, Jiangxi Province. In order to streamline authority and achieve practical results, it was also decided that the Ministry of Finance would be fully responsible for this matter. The Ministry of Finance began preparations for the establishment of the Administration in Shanghai last year, and once summoned leaders of the Shanghai rice industry, such as Gu Xinyi, to Beijing this month to discuss management methods. After returning to Shanghai, Gu stated that the government's measures were aimed at seeking food self-sufficiency, and the establishment of a large-scale storage warehouse in Jiujiang was no longer a problem. If this is the case, then the confusion in the rice market in the future can be permanently stabilized.

This Year's Loan Plan Handed Over to Each Director for Study, Shaanxi Cotton Sales Loans Increased to 850,000 Yuan: After the Traffic, Shanghai and other ten banks jointly organized the China Agricultural Loan Syndicate to aid the rural areas, it has been quite effective. He also mentioned that since Hubei implemented the new currency system policy, it has been quite effective, the market is stable, and various industries have become more active.

The Academia Sinica Held a Memorial Service for Ding Wenjiang Yesterday, with More Than 200 People Attending, Including Wu Tiecheng and Gu Mengyu, and President Cai Yuanpei Representing Zhou Ren as the Chief Mourner. Zhang Junmai and Cao Liangxia Also Gave Speeches. 102

The Academia Sinica held a memorial service for the late Secretary-General Ding Wenjiang at 2:00 PM yesterday, separately in Nanjing and Shanghai. President Cai Yuanpei personally served as the chief mourner. The details of the memorial service in Shanghai are recorded as follows: Venue Arrangement: The memorial service venue was in the auditorium of the Institute of Physics and Chemistry Laboratory of the Institute of Engineering on Bailinan Road. In the center was a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and a portrait of Ding Wenjiang. National flags and party flags were hung on the left and right, and the stage was filled with more than 20 wreaths presented from various parties. Many couplets and tents were hung on the four walls. The arrangement was simple and appropriate. At the entrance was a white cloth banner with the words "Memorial Service for the Late Secretary-General Ding Zaijun." There were also many greeters to guide and receive guests.

Attendees included Wu Tiecheng, Jiang Baili, Zhang Junmai, Gu Mengyu, Wang Jingqi, Hu Dunfu, Wang Yunwu, Zou Bingwen, Xu Xinliu, Yang Xiaoshu, Chen Guangfu, Cao Liangxia, Zhou Zijing, Xu Weiman, Zhuang Changgong, Zhao Shuyong, Qu Shaoqi, Gao Mengdan, Li Zuyu, Li Dachao, Huang Suchu, Zhang Diesheng, and other colleagues from the institute in Shanghai, approximately 200 people in total. Mayor Wu Cheng-tie, accompanied by Li Dachao, arrived at the meeting at around 2:00 PM. Due to other matters, he paid his respects to Ding's portrait and then left.

Portrait of Mr. Ding Wenjiang

Memorial Ceremony: The meeting began at 2:30 PM, with Cai Yuanpei (represented by Zhou Ren, Director of the Engineering Research Institute) as the chief mourner. The order was as follows: All stand in silence; Pay the highest respect to the party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; The chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will; Silence; Bow three times to Mr. Ding's portrait; Present wreaths; Silence (all factories stop for five minutes); President's speech; Report on Mr. Ding's life; Family's words of thanks; Ceremony completed.

Cai Yuanpei's Speech: President Cai Yuanpei of the institute was unable to attend due to hosting the Nanjing memorial service, so Zhou Ren read Cai's written speech on his behalf: "Today's meeting is a meeting for the Academia Sinica to mourn Mr. Ding Zaijun, the Secretary-General of the institute. Mr. Ding was a man who valued substance over form and hated formalism. In his will, he forbade the sending of obituaries and holding of condolence ceremonies. Therefore, we respect Mr. Ding's original intention and do not hold a large-scale joint memorial service, but only limit it to the colleagues of our institute, and hold it simultaneously in Beijing and Shanghai this afternoon to avoid the hardship of colleagues traveling back and forth. Mr. Ding was an expert in geology and also studied geography, anthropology, and eugenics. He was both knowledgeable and precise, and his reputation has long been established. He also had the ability to manage affairs, supported the Geological Survey, reorganized the Department of Geology at Peking University, and managed the Beipiao Coal Mine, all using scientific methods and achieving remarkable results. Mr. Ding was not yet fifty years old. If he had another ten or twenty years of work, his contributions to academic undertakings would be limitless. Unexpectedly, he fell ill and passed away. The loss to China's academic undertakings is immeasurable. Speaking within the institute, Mr. Ding served as the Secretary-General of our institute for less than two years, but his relationship and contribution to the institute were significant. For example, the organization of the Review Committee, the establishment of the Fund Custody Committee, and the demonstration of the budget proposals of various institutes have all laid a firm foundation for the institute. The improvement and expansion of various institutes within the institute also bear indelible merits. Furthermore, the plan for the Central Museum and the construction of the Cotton Textile Dyeing Experiment Hall are major projects of cooperation between the institute and other cultural institutions. Although completion is still pending, the rough outline has been established, which is also the result of Mr. Ding's efforts. If he had been given more time, I do not know what kind of progress he would have made. Now that Mr. Ding has suddenly left, is our institute not suffering a major blow? Mr. Ding was a pure scientist. He never tolerated the superstitions of religious figures or the fantasies of metaphysicians. Therefore, we dare not praise Mr. Ding with the immortal spirit passed down by religious figures and metaphysicians. We believe that Mr. Ding's immortal spirit will forever remain in the consciousness of those who die later. If we, who die later, can maintain the academic achievements that Mr. Ding has already built and enrich the academic achievements that Mr. Ding has not yet completed, then Mr. Ding will live on even though he is dead. When we colleagues mourn Mr. Ding, we must establish this ambition to be worthy of Mr. Ding and not betray our original intention of participating in the memorial service."

Report on Mr. Ding's Life: Zhuang Changgong, Director of the Institute of Chemistry, reported on Mr. Ding's life, stating that Mr. Ding was a native of Taixing, Jiangsu. He was exceptionally intelligent at an early age and had the reputation of being a child prodigy. At the age of fifteen, he studied in Japan, and then went to England and Germany to specialize in geology, earning a doctorate degree. At the age of twenty-five, he returned to China from Europe, detouring through the provinces of Yunnan and Guizhou to conduct on-site investigations of the geology of the southwest, pioneering the way for later scholars to investigate the geology of the southwest. In the first year of the Republic, he worked in the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, initiated the Geological Survey, served as the director of the institute himself, and concurrently served as a professor in the Department of Geology at Peking University. For ten years, he advocated investigation and made unique contributions. In the eleventh year of the Republic, he managed the Beipiao Coal Mine, and his achievements were remarkable. In the fifteenth year of the Republic, he left Beipiao and took office as the Shanghai Songhu Business Commissioner, and his political achievements were particularly remarkable. After the sixteenth year of the Republic, he returned to the north and served as a director of the Cultural Foundation and compiled a detailed map of China, and set off to investigate geology. After the eighteenth year of the Republic, he served as a professor at Peking University, until the twenty-third year when he took the position of Secretary-General of this institute. He wrote many books in his life, which are currently being compiled. Mr. Ding was not only a geologist and scientist, but also a manager and a leader. He was the most patriotic person. Now that Mr. Ding has passed away, it is a loss for the entire country of China.

Guest Speeches: Following the guest speeches, (1) Zhang Junmai said that Mr. Ding had both scientific knowledge and enthusiasm for management, which was truly rare and valuable. His life's work will last forever. To commemorate Mr. Ding, his colleagues should recognize his achievements. (2) Cao Liangxia said that Mr. Ding was not only scientifically profound but also morally noble. We should learn his noble morals so that China can be revived. Finally, Ding Wenhao, a member of the family, delivered a thank-you speech, and the meeting adjourned.

Lamentations from All Quarters: Yesterday, those who sent wreaths included Mayor Wu, Ye Zhuotang and Ling Hongxun of the China Science Society, Zou Bingwen, and more than 20 institutes, including the institute and various research institutes, which were all displayed in the venue. There were also many elegiac couplets and elegiac tents. Excerpts are as follows: Gu Mengyu: "If it were not for my old friend, perhaps I would not have arrived here at this time, to mourn and to bid farewell. Looking at Yunshan, I painfully remember the past and become an eternal regret." "And in the future, who will be able to use what they have learned to benefit the world? I am shocked and afraid to hear the sound of the Xiang River sobbing." Zhang Junmai: "Although science and metaphysics argue about right and wrong, the difference between righteousness and profit is the same as Zhu Xi and Lu Xiangshan." Wang Yunwu: "Geological research has turned into an elite spirit at the foot of the prison mountain. A genius cannot be obliterated and will forever leave a reputation to be broadcasted in Shengao." Zhang Yuanji: "The earth does not love treasures, but suffers. If he could fully display his talents, he would surely benefit our country." "When he reaches the age of knowing destiny, he should be able to serve in government, but why is he taken away like this? I still want to ask the heavens." Shi Zhipai: "He was brave in traveling and his ambitions far surpassed Xu Xiake." "Where did he die? Where was he buried? He traced the footsteps of Liu Ji Lun."

Decision to Establish a Scholarship: A reporter from Shanghai News asked Mr. Xu Weiman, the secretary of the institute, yesterday about the measures to commemorate Mr. Ding. According to him, it was decided to establish (1) a social science scholarship to commemorate Director-General Yang, and (2) a geology scholarship to commemorate Director-General Ding. It is currently estimated that Ding Xielin, Zhou Ren, Fu Sinian, Zhu Kezhen, Tao Mengzhi, and Xu Weiman will draft the measures, and it is planned to allocate 2,000 yuan each year to award to the geologist and social scientist in the country who has made the greatest contribution and conducted the most thorough research.

Joint Rent Reduction Association of Various Districts Presents to President Chiang: Please Issue a Clear Rent Reduction Order 103

The Joint Rent Reduction Association of various districts of this city, yesterday, again presented to President Chiang of the Executive Yuan, requesting the issuance of a rent reduction order. The original text stated: "Presented to request a swift order from the Municipal Government to issue a rent reduction order, in order to revitalize the market and stabilize society. It is humbly noted that since Shanghai has been affected by the global economy, all industries have declined, and industrial and commercial firms are closing down daily. Even those still operating are barely maintaining themselves. Unemployment and suicides are frequently seen. The suffering of the citizens cannot be fully described by pen and paper. Shanghai is the leading city in the country, a place where merchants from various countries gather. Therefore, during periods of economic prosperity, social development and goods also increase in price accordingly, and the living standards of the citizens also rise daily. Since the Shanghai War, the market has been sluggish everywhere, commerce has plummeted, unemployment has increased daily, and land prices have tragically fallen by half, with no one paying attention. However, all kinds of commodity prices have also fallen automatically, but most landlords disregard everything and stubbornly refuse to reduce rents, causing the suffering of all the city's tenants to not be alleviated at all. Since the establishment of the Rent Reduction Association, we have repeatedly appealed to the authorities, but not only is there no hope of rent reduction, but also an increase in tenants' lawsuits. Most landlords disregard humanity, using one-sided arguments to sue in court, using money and power to arbitrarily seize property. Although we previously received a reply from Your Excellency to be handled by the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Municipal Government has not yet expressed its position. Under the current market conditions, is it appropriate and reasonable for citizens to request rent reduction? Should the local government also devise methods to adjudicate? This Association dares to represent all the city's tenants and again earnestly requests Your Excellency to quickly determine a solution, or order the Shanghai Municipal Government to earnestly handle it. We have always admired Your Excellency's concern for the people's hardship, and we are confident that what is presented will be accepted. This would be a great kindness. Respectfully presented."

Telephone Problem Meeting: Yesterday, a Petition Was Submitted to the Public Works Department; Zhong Si Received Them and Promised a Written Reply, Stating that Dismantling Telephones Was a Foolish Move 104

The Special District Telephone Problem Committee of this city, due to the issue of telephone price increases in the concession, which have been approved by both the Public Works Department of the Public Concession and the Board of Directors of the French Concession, and scheduled to take effect on March 1st of this year, the deadline is approaching. Therefore, based on the decision of the first board meeting, representatives Lu Wenzhong, Zhang Yichen, Gu Wensheng, and Li Ao Kui, four people, were sent to the Public Works Department to submit a petition yesterday morning, requesting that the overall situation be considered and the new system be reconsidered to benefit the citizens. General Manager Zhong Si received them and replied, saying that the telephone company's new fee system has already been approved by the Public Works Department's board of directors, and it is difficult to overturn. If citizens express their opposition by dismantling telephones as a countermeasure, the company's future income will gradually decrease, and the remaining telephone users will inevitably increase their burden. Moreover, telephones are a convenient tool for communication, and anyone, for their own needs, would not want to be without them and suffer significant losses in their business. Therefore, I can assert that no one would take such a foolish move. The representatives of the committee, seeing that the petition yielded no results, will convene a meeting of representatives from various organizations after receiving the Public Works Department's written reply to discuss countermeasures. If necessary, a general meeting of citizens and users will be convened to discuss strict and effective countermeasures.

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau: Sponsors National Simple Life Insurance; Preferential Measures for Group Insurance 106

Since the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau launched simple life insurance, its business has developed rapidly due to its generous benefits and simple procedures. In order to promote group insurance, the bureau has established group insurance measures. All agencies, companies, banks, factories, schools, and other groups with 15 or more people who wish to take out insurance will be charged at 95% of the original amount to show preferential treatment. In recent days, various public and private groups have been eagerly requesting brochures and contacting the bureau for insurance, which has led to an increasingly busy workload for the bureau. It is also heard that the Ministry of Communications, in view of the fact that simple life insurance can directly protect the social economy and indirectly promote construction, which is of great benefit to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and should be promoted urgently, has issued a special order to all agencies and employees under its jurisdiction to join the insurance program. Currently, the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau, the Postal Bureau, the Telephone Bureau, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company are processing the joining procedures. In addition, the Ministry of Communications is also requesting the Executive Yuan to instruct all agencies and employees nationwide to join as a model.
