Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare: Yesterday's 7th Annual Meeting; President Kong Xiangxi Attended and Delivered the Opening Speech; Work Outline and This Year's Budget Approved 110

The Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare held its 7th annual meeting at the New Asia Restaurant yesterday at 3 PM. Attendees included President Kong Xiangxi, Vice President Luo Yunyan, Cai Hongtian representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, Chen Lengseng representing the Social Affairs Bureau, and members Wu Tiecheng, Liu Ruiheng, Zhao Jinqing, Li Dachao, Xu Shiying, Xiong Bingsan (represented by Li Liangzhao), Qu Wenliu, Xu Jianping, and Mrs. Liebert, representative of the American Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare, totaling over 200 people (presided over by President Kong).

Proceedings of the Meeting

At exactly 3 PM, the meeting commenced with the ringing of a bell. President Kong Xiangxi delivered the opening speech, followed by a report on association affairs by Executive Director Xu Jianping and a report on the financial situation by Accounting Group Leader Lin Kanghou. Representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau, including Chen Lengseng, and Xu Shiying then gave speeches. Subsequently, the implementation outline for the 25th year (1936) and the budget for the 25th year were approved. Executive committee members were elected. At 5:15 PM, the meeting adjourned with a group photograph and refreshments.

President's Address

Following proper protocol, President Kong Xiangxi delivered his opening speech, which stated, in brief: (1) Gratitude to All Sympathetic Individuals: Ladies and gentlemen, today is the day of our association's 7th annual meeting. Your presence and participation greatly encourages and deeply moves myself and my colleagues in the association. Our association was founded on April 4th of the 17th year of the Republic (1928). Now, we have more than seven years of history. In the beginning, our work focused mainly on rescuing children. However, now, our work has increasingly expanded. The general office is now divided into five groups: (1) General Affairs, (2) Relief, (3) Protection, (4) Hygiene, and (5) Education. Additionally, we have five affiliated institutions: (1) Philanthropic Clinic, (2) Philanthropic Nursery, (3) Philanthropic Training Institute, (4) Philanthropic Sanatorium, and (5) Chanbei Civilian Training Institute. These institutions provide medical care for children and carry out various practical works for the welfare of children. This is vastly different from the beginning. However, the association's ability to achieve these accomplishments is largely due to the assistance of many sympathetic individuals in society. They have supported the association in various ways with their spirit, their time, and their money. Therefore, the association is able to be where it is today. As the president of this association and one of the original founders, I must express my most sincere gratitude and deepest respect to these friends who have always supported the association. (2) Child Welfare is a National Salvation Undertaking: Ladies and gentlemen, recalling the beginning, why did Dr. Kuang Fuzhao, Dr. Luo Yunyan, Mrs. Guo Bingwen, Ms. Ding Shujing, Ms. Wang Liming, Mr. Gao Fengchi, and I initiate the Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare? Needless to say, we naturally wanted to use this organization to carry out child welfare. However, I would like to ask everyone to note that we are absolutely not handling child welfare as a charitable undertaking. Instead, we are handling it as a social and national salvation undertaking. Charitable undertakings are naturally commendable, but they are ultimately passive rather than active. Although a small part of the work carried out by this association is of a passive nature, such as rescuing disaster-stricken children in various places and saving abused maids, most of the work is of an active nature, such as promoting children's health, promoting children's education, promoting parental education, and promoting the use of the latest scientific methods to educate and nurture children nationwide. The association hopes not only to free children across the country from disaster and abuse, but also to ensure that children across the country have healthy bodies and sound minds in order to create a healthy Republic of China. Therefore, the work carried out by this association is naturally a far-reaching and national salvation undertaking, not just a passive charitable undertaking. Promoting children's happiness is naturally our goal, but our ultimate goal is to promote the happiness of the Chinese nation and complete the new construction of the Republic of China by promoting children's happiness. I would like to solemnly state this point to everyone at this annual meeting, and I believe that everyone will certainly be able to sympathize with and approve of this point. (3) The Importance Attached to Child Welfare in Various Countries Around the World: The foundation of a country naturally lies in its people. However, if a country does not first have healthy children, how can it produce healthy citizens? And how can it produce a healthy country? From this, we can know that if we want to build a healthy country, we must first cultivate healthy children. In other words, we must first complete the child welfare undertaking. Modern powerful countries around the world all attach great importance to child welfare. For example, the United States has a Children's Bureau, Austria has a Children's Protection Bureau, France has a Children's Protection Division, Italy has a General Association for the Protection of Mothers and Children, and Soviet Russia has a Headquarters for the Protection of Mothers and Children. In addition to establishing child protection agencies, governments around the world have successively formulated and promulgated many child protection laws, such as the Children Act in the United Kingdom, the Child Protection Act in the United States, the Child Rearing Act in France, the Juvenile Court Act in Germany, the Maternity and Child Act in Soviet Russia, the Maternity Protection Act in Italy, the Juvenile Act in Japan, and the Unified Regulations for Child Protection Undertakings in Belgium. Other countries attach great importance to child welfare. Looking back at our country, what is the situation? The reason why they are strong and we are weak lies in this. Recently, Stalin in Soviet Russia has incorporated all children in the country into the Children's League and the Youth League. Hitler in Germany has incorporated all children in the country into the Boy Scout Troop and the Youth Troop. Mussolini in Italy has incorporated all children in the country into the Balilla and the Vanguard. This fact should also be noted by those in China who are engaged in child welfare. After the Great War in Europe, President Hindenburg of Germany proposed a new budget in Congress, requesting more money to be spent on children. He solemnly said, "We have already lost everything in the World War. Now, we must never lose our children again." Thinking of China, in the past fifty years, we have lost many lands and many honors. How can we lose our children again? For the sake of our children, we should spend more money! (4) Conclusion: Today is the day of our association's 7th annual meeting. Our association sincerely hopes to take this opportunity to deeply reflect on the past and deeply strive for the future. My colleagues and I are aware of our limited knowledge and ability, so we are very willing to accept the criticisms and suggestions of all sympathetic individuals. We also ask those of you present today to not hesitate to correct us and give us guidance. This is what myself and my colleagues in the association earnestly hope for.

Mr. Xu's Speech

Xu Shiying's speech: Mr. Chairman, esteemed gentlemen, today is the 7th annual meeting of the Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare. I am able to participate, and I am honored that the assembly has called upon me to say a few words. The achievements of this association in the past seven years are evident to all, and there is universal praise. I need not elaborate further. Under the guidance of President Kong and Mrs. Kong, such progress has been made in these short seven years, which is truly admirable. Judging from the enthusiastic and inspiring atmosphere of today's meeting, and extrapolating from the past to the future, the future of the Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare is bright and can be anticipated. I, Shiying, am responsible for a part of social relief in the government. Regarding the operation of such a social organization that contributes to the public, benefits the nation, and helps the country, I feel very close and very envious in addition to admiration and prayers. In the past, the starting point of China's relief efforts was mostly based on sympathy, and it was not felt to be a sacred duty. The effect was mostly temporary and passive almsgiving, rather than a permanent and active cultivation of the strength of the country and the nation. The target was often scattered, and the organization was often lax. There was little division of labor and cooperation to achieve maximum efficiency. In recent decades, there have been scientifically managed charitable organizations and relief functions that go deep into society and focus on production. Everyone has come to realize that almsgiving cannot cultivate poverty and weakness, and has further carefully selected relief targets so that social forces can be used more permanently for the benefit of the country and the nation. This is what Shiying deeply admires and is comforted by. Among all these social organizations, the Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare is the most representative one. I will not elaborate on the importance of child relief, but in my humble opinion, the recent three to five decades of the Chinese nation may be more important in history than any era. Today's children can be said to be the masters of this stage. Therefore, it goes without saying that everyone in China today should do their best to carry out child welfare work. I hope that this annual meeting will take on the responsibility of leadership, so that all people in the country, regardless of gender, age, or status, can directly or indirectly become members of the child welfare team, inherit the past and usher in the future, and have a new atmosphere. In this sense, allow Shiying to once again congratulate the Chinese Philanthropic Association for Child Welfare on its future success. Confucius said, "Treat the elderly of your own family in the way they should be treated, and extend that treatment to the elderly of other families; treat the young of your own family in the way they should be treated, and extend that treatment to the young of other families." Although Shiying is old, I dare not ask you to treat the elderly of your own families, but I will always follow and strive to treat the young of your families, even though my strength is limited. Thank you all.

The French Municipal Council Applied for Land Tax; Wu Honggen Argued with the Articles of Association Notice; The Notice Clearly Stated that Chinese People Would Not Be Charged Taxes; Gu Shouxi and Others Appeared in Court for Unsuccessful Mediation 111

The tax office of the French Municipal Council recently stated that a piece of land located at No. 1412, Xiafei Road, inside the lane, with French certificate number 12767 B, measuring two mu, one fen, seven li, and six hao, along with the buildings on it, is owned by local Wu Honggen. The land price was estimated at 34,000 yuan per mu in 1934. According to 8 per thousand, the land tax was levied. The land tax due for the three periods from 1933 to 1935 was a total of 353 yuan, 2 jiao, and 8 fen. In addition, the house tax for May and June of last year was 39 yuan, of which 24 yuan and 8 jiao is still owed. From July to October, the total of 4 months is 78 yuan, totaling 102 yuan. The total amount owed is 456 yuan, 1 jiao, and 2 fen. Because the landlord Wu Honggen delayed and refused to pay, Gu Shouxi, Fei Xizhen, Yao Zhaodi, Yuan Jiahuan, and other lawyers were commissioned by Jia Tang (phonetic translation of the French Municipal Council's legal advisor) of the French Municipal Council to file a lawsuit with the Civil Division of the Special Second Court in accordance with the law. Yesterday afternoon at 3 o'clock, Judge Guo Huaipu summoned both parties in the Civil Division Seven Court to conduct a preliminary mediation. The applicant, the French Municipal Council, was represented by lawyer Gu Shouxi in court, and the respondent, Wu Honggen, was represented by lawyer Chen Wenxiang. First, the applicant's representative lawyer stated the case and the reasons for the mediation application. The respondent presented the articles of association and Shanghai Daoyin (道尹) and Special Envoy for Foreign Affairs of Jiangsu Province Yang Xiaochuan's notice issued when the French Concession was expanded in 1914 as reasons for their defense. According to Article 6 of the notice, "Chinese people residing in the French Concession and Wai Malu (外馬路), with cultivated land and houses, and houses of equal status, will not be charged donation taxes and other similar donations, and per capita tax regulations." The respondent's land had never been taxed since the concession was opened. As for the houses, which were old-style bungalows, 4 yuan and 9 jiao had always been paid per period and delivered on time, with the donation tickets issued. The respondent could not accept all of the applicant's requests. The applicant's representative lawyer also stated that when the concession was leased, it was all wilderness and farmland. The stipulation that farmland and houses on it would not be taxed was not the basis claimed by the respondent. The French consulate or the French embassy had records and original documents of the stipulations at that time, which could be submitted to the court for inspection. After verifying the words, the court declared that the mediation was unsuccessful and would be heard again. Then the court adjourned.

The Tongchun Garden Teahouse at No. 43, Maohai Road, suddenly caught fire at about 1:00 PM yesterday. The fire spread rapidly and was beyond control. Case of the Zhao Feng Pawnshop Partner Stealing Goods and Pawning Them Back 113

Two of Three Suspects Were Arrested, One Escaped; The Fraud and Embezzlement Case Was Concluded. The Zhao Feng Pawnshop at No. 102, Xujiahui Road, French Concession, was opened by Guo Liangji (46 years old) from Zhejiang. He hired Zhao Xianlu (age unknown), Wang Yingjie (28 years old), and Cai Jixiao (17 years old), all from the same hometown, to manage the package room. Unexpectedly, Zhao, Wang, and Li recently came up with a novel idea and colluded to steal the goods from the package rack and pawn them outside. They then entrusted others to pawn the stolen goods back at the Zhao Feng Pawnshop (the money was divided up and spent). Only now was it discovered that after checking the package room's goods and books, it was found that Zhao and the others had started stealing and pawning goods from May 1st of last year to December 28th, totaling 288 cases, with a total value of 2,548 yuan. The shop owner immediately reported the information to the French police for investigation. Unexpectedly, Zhao and the others were well-informed and fled together. Subsequently, detectives Gao Hongxuan and Hou Benyong began an investigation and learned that Zhao and the others had fled to No. 100, Hefeng Road, Wusong Town in the city. On the 14th of this month, they rushed to Wusong and requested the assistance of the local public security bureau. At 5:00 PM, they went to the address and only arrested Wang Yingjie and Cai Jixiao. Zhao Xianlu had already fled after hearing the news. Wang and Cai were then taken back to the French police station and sent to the Special Second Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Chen Pusheng presided over the trial in the Criminal Division Eight Court. Police lawyer Yuan Jiahuan stated the case and filed a lawsuit based on the fraud crime in Article 339 of the Criminal Code. Then, the plaintiff stated the process of discovering the defendants' collusion in stealing and pawning the goods back. After questioning Wang and Cai, they confessed to the collusion. Wang admitted to dividing up 1,110 yuan, and Cai admitted to dividing up 200 yuan. They also confessed that Zhao Xianlu divided up 302 yuan. Finally, the police lawyer argued that the defendants were not only guilty of fraud, but also had related embezzlement in their business, and requested strict punishment according to law. After verifying the words in court, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentence for the 25th. The two defendants were returned to custody.

Debt Collection Leads to Injury: Madam Lin Xiao Fortuitously Avoids Miscarriage; Chen Tongbiao Fined Fifteen Yuan 115

Madam Lin Xiao, a Chaozhou woman residing at No. 12, Tongyi Lane, Jing'an Temple Road, had previously deposited 10,000 yuan in cash with the Sanxing Real Estate Company at No. 348, Edward Road, with the understanding that it could be withdrawn at any time. Recently, needing funds, she went to the company's manager, Zhang Yangzhou, at No. 3, Lane 220, Yanping Road, to withdraw the money. However, despite several attempts, she received nothing. On the 2nd of the month, accompanied by her relative Lin Li, she went to Zhang's house again at 9:10 AM. Zhang was not there, and Zhang's nephew, Chen Tongbiao, came out to greet them. Unexpectedly, a conflict arose during the conversation, and Chen violently shoved Madam Lin Xiao, causing her to fall to the ground. As she was nine months pregnant, she sustained injuries. She reported the incident to the Gordon Road Police Station and was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment, being discharged only on the 5th. She then requested the police to prosecute Chen. The police repeatedly summoned Chen, but he failed to appear. Consequently, they petitioned the First Special District Court for a warrant. Yesterday, the warrant was served to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian explained the above situation, prosecuting Chen for causing injury under Article 277 of the Criminal Code, and stated that the plaintiff could not appear in court today as she had just given birth. Lin Li then recounted the circumstances of the incident. When questioned, Chen Tongbiao claimed, "I did not push the plaintiff down. The three of them beat me. I used my hands to block them, and the plaintiff was wearing high heels and accidentally fell. I was also injured," presenting a medical certificate as evidence. Judge Zhan Liangce reviewed the testimonies and sentenced Chen Tongbiao for causing injury, imposing a fine of fifteen yuan, commutable to one day of labor for each yuan. Chen expressed his willingness to accept the sentence.

Drug Trafficking Offense: Another Drug Trafficker Apprehended; Police File Charges Against "Hemp-Faced" Teahouse Owner, etc. Public Concession Judge Orders Handling According to Regulations, No Need for Transfer 117

Sha Daqi, the squad leader of the Detective Division of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently apprehended a drug trafficker named Cao Zhongfan and discovered a pre-printed letter stating that morphine could be purchased from a "hemp-faced" teahouse owner at Room 26, Huzhou Inn, North Shanxi Road. He reported this to the bureau chief and, in coordination with Xie Guisheng, a Chinese detective of the Huishi Police Station, went to arrest the teahouse owner, Zhang Delin (the "hemp-faced" teahouse owner mentioned in the letter), a Huzhou native working as a tea server at the inn. They also apprehended Di Qingsheng from Shaoxing, Xu Maotou from Suzhou, and Chen Guitao and Zhang Dianchen from Shaoxing. Two ledgers were also found under Chen's hat, which Public Security Bureau personnel stated were records of drug sales. All were taken back to the police station and sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang Risheng continued the hearing in the Fifth Criminal Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu filed charges under Article 263 of the Criminal Code. Representatives from the Public Security Bureau arrived in court, requesting a transfer of the case. Judge Huang stated that since the police had already filed a public prosecution, the case must go through the judicial process. Furthermore, the court would handle the case according to the anti-smoking and anti-drug regulations, which were the same as those in the inland areas. Therefore, the case did not need to be transferred for the time being. If the Public Security Bureau had sufficient evidence, they could submit it for the court's reference and assist the police in the investigation. If it was determined after the verdict that there were other offenses, evidence could be submitted for prosecution. The Public Security Bureau representative requested a written notice be sent to the Public Security Bureau and then withdrew. After questioning each defendant, Judge Huang, considering the case involved drug trafficking, instructed the police detectives on the points to be investigated and then adjourned the hearing.

Liu-Wu Adultery Case: Verdict Announced in Court Yesterday; Liu Xi's Criminal Suit Withdrawn by Liu Zirong; Wu Wenxiang Sentenced to One Year and Six Months, Appeals 118

The sensational Liu-Xi/Wu Wenxiang love affair was adjudicated by the District Court yesterday. Wu Wenxiang was found guilty of seduction and sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Wu, dissatisfied with the verdict, immediately announced his appeal. Liu Xi's charges were withdrawn by her husband, Liu Zirong, in court, and Liu Xi was taken away by lawyer Tu, regaining her freedom. The preliminary trial concluded at this point. The details of the interrogation are as follows: Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the gallery of the Third Court was already full. Latecomers found no space to stand, and all stood on tiptoe waiting. When the bell rang three times, Judge Shao Qinzhi, Prosecutor Tang Rushu, and Clerk Xie Xirong entered the court and took their seats. The private prosecution lawyer Shan Yuhua, representing the plaintiff Liu Zirong, and the two lawyers Chao Kun and Tu Kunfan, representing the first defendant Liu Xi, and the lawyer Dong Banggan, representing the second defendant Wu Wenxiang, successively appeared in court. The court asked Liu Zirong about the extent of the out-of-court settlement. Liu replied that it was generally agreed upon, unconditional divorce, and the 5,000 yuan she brought out had also been arranged, but the expenses had not been discussed. The judge said, "Observing your settlement, neither party is sincere. Further delays are very detrimental to the defendant." Lawyer Tu rose and stated, "Requesting the court to grant Liu Xi bail and extend the period by ten days or a week to facilitate direct negotiations with the plaintiff for a smoother settlement." Prosecutor Tang Rushu immediately expressed his opposition, stating that the facts of the case were quite clear and simple. The settlement was a civil matter and should not involve criminal proceedings, which would affect the credibility of the court. Further delays were inappropriate, and the judge should promptly render a verdict. Judge Shao said to the defendant's lawyer, "The court could have concluded at the beginning, but further investigation was needed." Lawyer Tu rose and stated, "Requesting the court to allow our lawyers to take Liu Xi to the waiting room to discuss the settlement with Liu Zirong." The judge approved, and Liu Xi, Liu Zirong, and others left the court. After half an hour, the hearing continued. The court asked Liu Zirong if he could settle. Liu replied, "Withdrawing the charges against Liu Xi, and Wu Wenxiang should be severely punished according to law." Lawyer Shan rose and stated that the private settlement had been agreed upon (reportedly 5,500 yuan), and the money should be handled by Lawyer Tu. The clerk was requested to record it. As the private suit had been resolved and Liu Xi's charges had been withdrawn by Liu Zirong, Lawyer Shan and Lawyers Tu and Chao left first, and Liu Xi was taken away by Lawyer Tu. The court then said to Liu Zirong, "Please describe the circumstances of the discovery again." Liu replied, "I went to the police at 7:00 AM that day and broke into the pavilion room on the second floor, where I saw Liu Xi and Wu Wenxiang sleeping in the same bed. They were not ashamed and said it didn't matter, let's go to court." The court asked, "Did Wu Wenxiang seduce Liu Xi, or did Liu Xi seduce the chauffeur?" Liu replied, "Perhaps Wu Wenxiang seduced her, but she must have agreed to run away later. After Liu Xi and others left, the maids A Bao and A Jin also resigned, supposedly because Wu Wenxiang said to A Bao, 'We're leaving, so should you.'" Before Wu Wenxiang left, he flirted at my house, making it clear that he was fond of the young mistress, so I stopped him. The court asked, "Are there any civil matters with Wu Wenxiang now?" Liu replied, "No, I only seek his punishment." At this point, Prosecutor Tang Rushu rose and gave his argument. The court then instructed the defense to begin. Lawyer Dong rose and stated that in this case, Liu Xi and Wu Wenxiang were jointly liable. Now that Liu Xi's charges have been withdrawn by Liu Zirong, Wu Wenxiang should be declared not guilty. Wu Wenxiang's position was that of a servant, and he would not dare to have an affair with the mistress. Liu Xi was a married woman, not comparable to Huang Hui Ru's love affair with Lu Geng Rong. Moreover, Xi came from a wealthy family, how could she abandon her happy family to be in love with a poor chauffeur? If the court believes Wu Wenxiang is guilty, please grant him a suspended sentence. The court then asked Wu Wenxiang, "Did you rent the house?" Wu replied, "No." The court said, "Don't be evasive. Liu Xi's diary states that the day after renting the house, your sworn brother came to borrow money, and you told them the address. Now the court is giving you a chance, you should confess the truth." Wu Wenxiang refused to admit to the adultery with Liu Xi. The court, having heard the testimony, found the facts of the case to be very clear and declared the case closed, immediately sentencing Wu Wenxiang for adultery to one year and six months of imprisonment. Wu, dissatisfied with the verdict, was ordered to present the reasons and appeal according to law. He was ordered to be remanded in custody pending further instructions.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau Increases Rental Fees for Intercoms: Shanghai-Minhang Company Requests Exemption from Increase of Over Five Times the Original Rate 119

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau has announced an increase in rental fees this month, with some rates increasing by four or five times. Various users find such a significant increase unaffordable. It was learned yesterday that the Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Long-Distance Bus Company on Guohuo Road in this city has an intercom with a monthly rental fee of 10 yuan. Now, the monthly fee is to increase to 51 yuan, more than five times the original rate. The company sent a letter yesterday requesting an exemption from the increase, or else they will have the intercom removed immediately. The intercom lines are maintained by the users themselves, and the bureau's work is simpler than for ordinary telephones. Moreover, users are responsible for the wiring and installation costs when requesting installation. This significant increase seems unfair.

Recently, many Chinese and foreign industrialists have jointly raised funds to prepare for the Shanghai International Exposition, which will be open to all nationalities and will include agriculture, industry, commerce, and education, gathering the essence of all nations for the public to view. The scale of the exhibition, the breadth of the solicitation, and the grand purpose are unprecedented in China. It is said that the location has been selected in the eastern district of the Public Concession on a plot of land in the middle section of Yangshupu Road, bordering the road to the north and the Huangpu River to the south, covering an estimated area of over 200 mu. The internal construction has been entrusted to the local Qiming Architectural Firm and the British-owned Yuhua Foreign Company, who are designing and drawing plans. Construction is expected to begin soon. The exhibition period is tentatively set for two months, with the opening scheduled for June of this year. Chinese and foreign businesses have already begun contacting the organizing committee to arrange for exhibits.

The *North-China Daily News* reports that there are plans to hold a large-scale exhibition in Shanghai in June or July of this year, covering the three sectors of industry, commerce, and education in Shanghai. According to Mr.鲍维尔, the civil engineer who will be supervising the construction of the venue, 2 million square feet of land has been rented on the Bund of the Public Concession for the venue. He spent five months handling the preliminary technical equipment. The drawings for the venue buildings have been completed by a German architect.

The *Shanghai Times* reports that the Shanghai Exhibition, which has been promoted for a long time, will be located on the old site of the Sanxin Yarn Factory on the Bund of Yangshupu. An office will be set up at No. 356, near Jing'an Temple Road and Ma Huo Road, in the coming days. Construction of the venue buildings will begin in March, and it is expected to open in early June. The exhibition period is tentatively set for June and July. If the results are good, there is a possibility of extending the exhibition. Negotiations are currently underway with the Municipal Council. It is said that the Council is very supportive of the plan, and the Works Department, Health Department, and Fire Department are willing to cooperate. The construction cost of the buildings is approximately 200,000 yuan. The Municipal Council's taxes on the property are approximately 3,000 yuan per month. The license fee is currently unknown. Once the buildings are completed, they will be rented to local businesses to display industrial, commercial, and educational items. The exhibition will also display items from other parts of China and overseas. The venue will also include a large amusement park with various games, such as dramas, movies, and dances, as well as various food stalls, which will also be contracted out. The admission fee is approximately 2 jiao or 2.5 jiao.

Lin Kanghou Delivers Speech on Behalf of the Presidium; Zhang Qun, Chen Jie, and Others Send Congratulatory Telegrams

The commemorative ceremony for Mr. Wang Xiaolai's 30th anniversary in Shanghai and his 50th birthday, initiated by Mayor Wu and others, was held at the Hu She on Guizhou Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. Prominent figures from all walks of life, including Yu Qiaqing, Zhu Ziqiao, Chen Aishi, Chu Minyi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Lin Kanghou, Xu Shiying (represented by Huang Bodu), Pan Gongzhan, Wang Binyan, Yan Esheng, Wang Yansong, and Lu Jingshi, totaling over a thousand people, attended to offer their congratulations. After the formal ceremonies, Lin Kanghou delivered a speech on behalf of the presidium, followed by Wang Xiaolai's report on his 30 years in Shanghai, which stated that he was born on December 24th of the Bingxu year of the Guangxu reign. He began his business career in his youth, engaging in silk, tea, cocoon, and yarn, and also devoted himself to national, local, and social causes. He had five major endeavors in his life: National economy and people's livelihood, Local community affairs, Public welfare and charity, Educational and cultural endeavors, Industrial production. He stated that his aspirations have remained unchanged and consistent throughout. Yu Qiaqing then gave a speech, stating that Mr. Wang Xiaolai possessed these five major endeavors, and colleagues could follow in his footsteps. The only thing that could not be emulated was Mr. Wang's Heaven-bestowed blessing of a full house of descendants, which his colleagues could only admire from afar. The audience laughed. Chen Aishi then gave a speech, saying that when the National Revolutionary Army was about to arrive in Shanghai, the silver and money circles in Shanghai secretly raised funds, and Mr. Wang Xiaolai was the most active in this effort. The fact that the National Revolutionary Army was able to establish its capital in Nanjing was due to Mr. Wang's efforts. Yu Zuoting, Chu Minyi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others then gave speeches in succession. The ceremony concluded at 5:00 PM. Diplomats Zhang Qun, Chief Chen Jie, Relief Director Xu Shiying, and Cheng Yanqiu sent congratulatory telegrams. Mr. Wang's friends were all over the world, resulting in a constant stream of cars at the entrance of Hu She, making it a grand occasion.

Gang Members Turn on Each Other: Detectives Investigate the Truth Behind the Gang; Qian Cries Out "Zhou Da is Shooting!"; Qi Lao Dives into the River with His Gun; Seven-Year-Old Child Comes from Jiangbei 122

On the night of the 9th of this month, an internal dispute broke out among gang members at No. 63, Tong'an Lane, Matthews Road, resulting in gang members turning on each other. Jiangbei gangster Lü Zhenmin was shot and killed, and Yang Bangjie was wounded. Chinese and Western detectives from the responsible police station arrested a large number of suspected men and women in the case, including Yang Jinshi, Chen Bishu, and Qian Jinshan, a total of eleven people, and sent them to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention, as previously reported. It is now learned that after the court hearing was postponed the other day, the Chinese and Western detectives in charge of the case interrogated the suspects. The tenth defendant, Qian Jinshan, revealed that there were other accomplices hiding on boats in the river at Lan Road, Yangshupu. The Western detective chief Li Teh-hua, detective Zhu Mengwei, Zhu Hanbo, detective Pi Shaochang and others, along with Qian Jinshan, went to arrest them at 9 PM the day before yesterday. They also notified the Yangshupu police station in charge. As soon as the Chinese and Western detectives arrived at the riverbank of Lan Road, there were six or seven Jiangbei boats parked in the river. Not knowing which boat the gang members were hiding on, they were about to ask Qian to identify the boat to facilitate the arrest when Qian, cunning as he was, suddenly shouted, "Zhou Da is shooting!" Hearing the alarm, two gang members from the boat, armed with weapons, jumped into the river and tried to escape by swimming. The Chinese and Western detectives ordered them to stop, but they ignored the order. The detectives then fired at them, firing a total of nine shots, none of which hit. As a result, the two gang members managed to escape. Only Jiangbei native Zhao Cheng, the woman Qi Zhang, and her ten-year-old son Qi Buyou were arrested on the two boats, along with a seven-year-old girl who had been kidnapped. While the Chinese and Western detectives were searching for the accomplices, one of the gang members who had escaped by swimming, named Zhou Buyun, climbed out of the river and onto the opposite bank of Heilong Road. He was suddenly encountered by a Chinese constable No. 1949, who saw that Zhou was covered in water and had a white package in his hand, making him look suspicious. The constable also knew that detectives had been arresting thieves on the boats, so he ordered him to stop. Zhou ignored him and ran away. The constable then drew his gun and fired, hitting Zhou in the right leg. Zhou fell to the ground and was arrested, but the white package could not be found anywhere. The wounded bandit was sent to St. John's Hospital and then transferred to the police hospital for treatment. The arrested bandits Zhao Cheng and others were taken back to the police station. After investigation, it was learned that the other bandit who had escaped by swimming, named Qi Lao, was Qi Zhang's husband. It was also found that when the two bandits fled, they each carried a Mauser pistol with thirteen bullets. The guns and bullets were brought back to the police station. Yesterday morning, Zhao Cheng, Qi Zhang, and Qi Buyou were sent to the Eighth Court of the First Special Court, requesting that they be detained and tried together with the Yang Jinshi case. According to police lawyer Zhang Tianyin's statement, Qi Buyou was only ten years old, but the police had found that the defendants often used children to transport handguns when committing crimes, so he was suspected. The seven-year-old girl who was rescued claimed to have been kidnapped from Jiangbei. Because she could not state her name, she should be temporarily sent to the Women and Children Relief Association for care. When questioned, Zhao Cheng gave evasive answers. Qi Zhang confessed that the escaped Qi Lao was her husband. The seven-year-old girl was entrusted to her boat by Qian Jinshan from Jiangbei to be brought to Shanghai. Qi Buyou confessed that he had transported two handguns with another nine-year-old child. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the testimony and ordered Zhao Cheng and others to be detained and tried together on the 31st of this month. The girl was allowed to be sent to the Women and Children Relief Association for care.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Rewards 109 Crew Members: Each Receives One Month's Salary, Totaling 17,755 Yuan 124

Since the head of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was changed to a Chinese national, with Shen Jiyun taking the position, the company has focused on the fundamental goal of recovering navigation rights for Chinese. Foreign crew members who had been hired at high salaries were gradually replaced with Chinese crew members. However, when the four new Hai-class steamships sailed to Hong Kong, the Hong Kong government insisted on using foreign crew members in order to issue passenger licenses. Shen Jiyun considered this action to be insulting to China's national dignity. He would rather give up the passengers from Hong Kong and insist on employing Chinese crew members. After a few months, the performance of the Chinese crew members proved to be better than that of the foreign crew members. The Hong Kong government was impressed and allowed the Haiheng, Haili, and Haizhen ships to carry Hong Kong passengers, setting a precedent for Chinese shipowners. The British government had never heard of such a thing before and sent a telegram to Hong Kong to inquire, as this matter was of great importance to China's shipping industry. Shen also emphasized crew members being responsible for their duties in order to reduce the various dangers and losses at sea. Therefore, in 1934, he formulated rules for crew members' leave, punishment, and rewards, using two years of service as the standard. If a crew member did not take leave during the two years, they would be rewarded. If they wished to take leave, their salary would be deducted on a daily basis. Since the implementation of these rules, they have greatly benefited maritime operations. Now that the two-year period has expired, crew members who have not taken leave should be rewarded. After a review of the results, 109 crew members were found to be eligible for rewards, including 10 captains such as Yang Xin, 15 chief mates, 6 second mates, 24 river pilots, 17 chief engineers such as Feng Yuming, 16 first assistant engineers, 10 second assistant engineers, 1 third assistant engineer, and 10 telegraph operators. In accordance with Article 9 of the leave rules, the above 109 people will each be rewarded with one month's salary, totaling 17,755 yuan in national currency. The list has been prepared and submitted to the board of directors for review, and will then be forwarded to the company's treasury for payment in the coming days. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has not had a system of rewards and punishments for a long time. The implementation of the two-year work performance assessment and the awarding of bonuses is the first time.

Since the Ningbo Industrial Bank Restoration Preparatory Office received the order from the Ministry of Finance to issue 20% cash payments to the Ningbo Industrial Bank's depositors in batches, due to the large number of depositors and cumbersome procedures, the second batch of payments up to 500 yuan was only completed yesterday. This proposal by the creditors fulfills the responsibility of promoting national goods, and is also of great benefit to the creditors themselves. Therefore, the office consulted with the Guohuo Company, which also agreed and promised to proceed accordingly.

Thanks to the enthusiastic rescue of the charitable gentlemen on the sea, who generously contributed to the cause, we are deeply grateful and have nothing to repay. The City Health Bureau, in accordance with Article 14 of the "Provisional Regulations for the Administration of Physicians in this City, as Amended," which stipulates that "the business licenses held by traditional Chinese medicine practitioners should be audited and verified once a year from February 1st to the end of March, stamped and returned, and those who fail to submit for verification once within the time limit will be fined no more than five yuan," annually conducts an audit and verification of the registration certificates of traditional Chinese medicine practitioners within the prescribed time limit. Yan Zizhang, a dye merchant, was kidnapped on July 17th of the 18th year of the Republic of China at 2:20 a.m. After leaving the Dadong Dance Hall on Yinghua Street with a famous prostitute, he was about to step into his own car when several kidnappers suddenly appeared. Emergency Meeting of the Thermos Bottle Industry Association 134

The Thermos Bottle Manufacturing Industry Association recently convened an emergency meeting the day before yesterday to discuss relief measures for two major issues: the interruption of the source of the main raw material, domestic silver nitrate (i.e., silver powder), which affects the production of products, and the excessive cost of coal gas fuel (i.e., city gas). Gan Fengnan chaired the meeting as usual. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, and then the discussion of the cases was recorded below: 1. Regarding domestic silver nitrate, since the government explicitly ordered the reform of the legal currency system, raw silver can no longer be privately traded. This domestic industrial raw material will inevitably disappear from the market. However, the manufacture of our products relies entirely on silver nitrate as the only main raw material. Now that the source has been cut off, the impact on our industry's production is huge. How should we seek relief? Resolution: In this period of dumping of foreign goods and decline of domestic industries, our industry is planning to strive for development and cannot give up eating because of choking. The association should compile statistics on the annual demand of each factory of the industry and submit them to the government, requesting the allocation of raw silver. The association will prepare the price and collect it in order to manufacture it ourselves and maintain the industry. If necessary, representatives will be sent to Beijing to petition. 2. The annual coal gas fuel cost of each factory in the industry is huge, but the Shanghai City Gas Company not only charges exorbitant fees for fuel to the industry but also has extremely strict regulations. Although it has been repeatedly requested to reduce fuel costs, it has not been effective. How should this be handled? Resolution: In this situation of market depression and industry decline, this fuel cost accounts for almost 50% of all expenses, which is a major reason for the industry's depression. Since the request for reduction has not been effective, the association should plan to set up a joint self-operated coal gas factory or solicit specialized talents to study other substitutes in order to save expenses and reduce the cost of products. 3. Recently, the purchase prices of various raw materials have soared. Should the market price of our industry be raised to maintain capital? Resolution: A general meeting will be convened again before the spring opening to discuss it. 4. The non-member factories have been repeatedly urged to pay the monthly fee in accordance with the law, but they still refuse to pay. How should they be dealt with? Resolution: If they still refuse to pay after three months, legal action will be taken in accordance with the law. The meeting adjourned at more than 7 o'clock.

Yesterday's Western League Group A Soccer Match: Youyou Wins Over Jewish Team with a Score of 6 to 1: Jewish Team Played with Only Nine Players and Suffered a Miserable Defeat: Due to the Severe Cold Weather, Only About Thirty Fans Arrived 144

Youyou vs. Jewish team, the Group A league match was held yesterday at Shenyuan Stadium. The Jewish team lacked manpower and played with only nine players. Due to the disparity in strength between the two sides, the match became one-sided. Youyou won over Jewish team with a score of 6 to 1, and Jewish team suffered a miserable defeat. Yesterday's weather was severely cold, and the number of fans could be counted on one's fingers, with only about thirty people. The details are as follows:

Wang Nanzhen Scores the First Goal

As soon as the battle began, the Jewish team kicked off. Halfway through, Liang Shuye intercepted the ball, sent it far to the front line, and Zhen He Nanzhen shot three times, but failed to score. Feng turned the ball on the baseline, and the pass was just right. Zhen He added a shot, just hitting the arms of the goalkeeper Zhabo. Yuxiang did the same, but it was all in vain. Jewish center M. Greenberg launched a solo western invasion, but it was only a flash in the pan. After the ball hovered in the Jewish team's territory several times, Harry Sthing stumbled on the ball. Liu Shizan caught up and crossed the ball. Wang Nanzhen waited for the right moment, slightly nudged the ball, and it entered the net. Youyou scored the first goal, less than fifteen minutes after the start of the match. The kickoff from the center line immediately returned to the Jewish team's territory. Yuxiang and Nanzhen shot twice, but Zhabo rescued them from danger. Nanzhen got a corner kick opportunity, but Ping missed it himself. Nanzhen committed a foul and was penalized. Feng sent the ball out, and Yuxiang shot, just hitting the crossbar, and Zhabo turned it into a corner kick. Yong Sen opened the kick, and Shizan landed on the ball, deflecting it away. It hit the bullseye again, making the score 2 to 0.

First Half: Jewish Team Scores Zero

After the kickoff, Feng killed into the enemy's formation, forcing a corner kick. The Jewish team launched a counterattack once, but was still sent out. Zhen He is worthy of being an expert, dribbling past the front and rear guards, reaching the front of the goal, but unfortunately hit the post and bounced back. Youyou launched another siege, and Shizan took advantage of the chaos to kick the ball into the net again, scoring 3 to 0. The Jewish team tried hard to counterattack, but could not enter Youyou's territory at all. Hei Tan got the ball from Feng, but his shot missed the goal. Zhalin committed a foul, and instead of catching up, he kicked the ball with all his strength, just hitting the corner of the net. Then the Jewish team got an opportunity to attack, but Jiang Shanqing forced a corner kick. Daobo Laiji took the kick, and Rongcai kicked it out, but before he could make any progress, the whistle blew for half-time. In the first half, Youyou scored four goals, and the Jewish team scored zero.

6 to 1: Youyou Defeats the Enemy

Changing sides to fight again, the ball still hovered in the Jewish team's territory. Zhen He and Feng both shot, but both went over the crossbar. Hao Xueke dribbled the ball to attack, but as soon as he crossed the center line, he was intercepted by Zhen Xiang. Yuxiang dribbled the ball, and Zhabo撲地rescued him. The ball rolled into the net from his arm, making the score 5 to 0. The three forwards of the Jewish team advanced together, but Lao Jiang accidentally committed a foul and was penalized with a penalty kick. M. Zhabolin took the kick, just hitting the corner of the net, and Rongcai could not save it. Youyou lost a goal. Zhen He and Nanzhen fired in succession, but were both saved by Zhabo. Daobo Laiji attacked along the side, and Jiang Shanqing arrived from outside the Guan, forcing a corner kick. Youyou attacked again, and Yong Sen headed the pass, and Hei Tan's iron leg flew at the ball, sending it into the net again, making the score 6 to 1. The Jewish team was defeated.

Three Games in the Zilin Cup Soccer Tournament: Youyou, Donghua, and Qinghua All Win 146

Youyou B Wins Over Aurora: 5 to 2

Donghua B Wins Over Apellon: 9 to 3

Qinghua Wins Over Yousheng: 5 to 2

Youyou B Wins Over Aurora: In the second match of the Zilin Cup, Youyou faced Aurora yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at Hongkou Park. Aurora was a mixture of Chinese and Western athletes, while Youyou was a strong team in the previous cup competitions. Therefore, yesterday's match was quite exciting. In the first half, because Aurora's center Luo Gans did not play, Youyou scored four goals in a row. Although Aurora pulled back two goals in the second half, it was of no avail due to too many goals conceded. As a result, Youyou eliminated Aurora with a score of 5 to 2.

Donghua B Wins Over Apellon: In the Zilin Cup match, Donghua B faced Apellon yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at Jiaozhou Park on Jiaozhou Road. Donghua was eliminated in the preliminary cup competition after losing to Youyou, so they put all their efforts into the Zilin Cup. Therefore, yesterday's match was played with all the troops mobilized, attacking and defending together, and they were exceptionally hardworking. Although they deployed against the wind in the first half, they were still able to score four goals. In the second half, deploying with the wind, Apellon naturally felt even more overwhelmed. As a result, Donghua won with a score of 9 to 3.

Qinghua Wins Over Yousheng: In the Zilin Cup match, Qinghua faced Yousheng yesterday at the First Hongkou Stadium. In the first half, Qinghua's Ge Xizuo scored a penalty kick, taking the lead with a score of 1 to 0. In the second half, Yousheng's Chen Yan leveled the score. Soon after, Ge Xizuo broke Yousheng's goal from 20 yards away. Li Songyun again tied the score at 2 to 2. Later, Qinghua's Ge Xielin and the three forwards each made contributions, and Qinghua won over Yousheng with a score of 5 to 2.

Cheng Yuhuai Returns Home After Completing Studies in Germany 162

Cheng Yuhuai, a native of She County, Anhui Province, is 26 years old. In 1928, he transferred from Tongji University to the University of Göttingen in Germany, majoring in mathematics for five years, and obtained a doctorate degree. He then studied at the University of Zurich in Switzerland and the University of Hamburg in Germany. He has been away for nine years. Due to his excellent academic performance, he has successively obtained the Anhui Provincial Scholarship and the scientific research subsidy from the China Education and Culture Foundation. He is now returning to China to take up a position at Peking University. He has traveled to Denmark, Rome, Paris, Lyon, and other places to conduct inspections and will arrive in Shanghai in the latter half of this month.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1)(5)(6) 163

— Original by Louisa M Aleott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Huakunlan was the only person Pang Taomo felt he could trust to work in his "shop." So he taught Kunlan how to find eggs and deliver them safely, satisfied with just an apple or a date as a reward for his labor. The morning after Donn showed his strange expression on Sunday, Kunlan contributed the fruits of his labor from a major decision, saying to his master:

"Only two."

"Worse every day; Damn old hen, I've never seen one like it," Taomo roared, recalling the heyday when he often had six to collect, which made him smile often, truly unbearable to look back on. "Ah, put them in my hat, give me a little lead pencil, I want to write them down."

Kunlan then climbed onto a large basket and looked at the top of the machine, where Taomo had placed paper and pen. Kunlan said, "There's also a lot of money here."

"No, there isn't. How could I put money there randomly," Taomo replied.

"I see them—one, four, eight, two dollars," Kunlan insisted, still unable to figure out the numbers clearly.

"You're really an annoying little trickster!" Taomo said and climbed up the ladder himself to get the lead pencil, but almost fell down because he actually saw four bright, shiny four-dollar coins arranged neatly, with a piece of paper on top stating "For Pang Taomo" to avoid any mistakes.

"Heaven and earth are turned upside down!" Taomo shouted, then picked them up and immediately rushed into the big house, shouting frantically, "Everything is fine! The money is here! Where's Ned?"

Although the major short sellers have already made profits, they are too big to fail and cannot make up for it, so they also feel difficulties. London is the main market for black tea trade. The prosperity or decline of the tea market there is of great importance to the world tea industry. Piece Goods: Woolen Cloths of the Past Year 184

The year of 24 has passed in the blink of an eye. The changes in the woolen cloth market situation during this year are also quite considerable. Now I will briefly describe the entire process for the reference of both insiders and outsiders.

January: Because it was close to the end of the old lunar year and the settlement period, both overt and covert funds were tight. It was extremely difficult to recover debts, which were greatly discounted compared to the year 23. Customer accounts in Nanjing and Hankou were even worse, and many orders from foreign clothing stores were returned. Woolen cloths also successively saw a decline in orders. Only "Ren" character woolen cloth was almost completely snapped up and saw a unique surge in price. 1005's eighteen and twenty-four colored riding breeches cloth also sold well and increased in price. Overcoat cloth suffered the most losses because the weather was mild, unlike a typical winter, and sales were sluggish, resulting in a large amount of inventory being left unsold.

February: The opening price of the red market was very flat. Most were cheaper than the closing price of the previous month. Only the "Jue" character "Ren" character woolen cloth and twilled bunting remained firm and expensive, while everything else declined. The Yuanbao business in this street was smoother than in previous years because the opening price of the red market was flat and standardized, avoiding the bad habit of haggling. Most of the direct tribute cloths and plain serges had already been defeated by Japanese goods. Although the price of Western plain serge was cheap, it was still not easy to sell.

March: This month, the woolen cloth trade was very prosperous. Stores, foreign clothing tailors, hat workshops, etc. in this street, as well as large and small customers from Beiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, Hankou, Nanchang, Changsha, Guiyang, and the Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, all made large purchases. Only the Sichuan customers' purchasing power remained sluggish, but the Sichuan customers also made some minor purchases. Plain serge, Yuan direct tribute, plain Walter, flannel suit cloth, Zhong-something-Hai Ling Peng, patterned foreign cloth, bunting, etc., all sold very well. Single-sided "open water" rice market sales were also active. Unfortunately, the credit price was even weaker than in February. The reason for this was still the sluggish market, tight funds, and long turnover periods for earlier orders. Different purchasing costs led to competition and chaos.

April: Cloth prices fell eight or nine out of ten times. No one in the industry hoped for an increase. Most only hoped to maintain stability, which would be considered fortunate. Although summer goods needed for summer sales were gradually appearing on the market, the market situation was still extremely bad. Recovering loans was quite difficult. Returned orders from Western clothing stores flooded the market. Bankruptcies and closures continued in both local and out-of-town areas. The tightness of funds and the difficulty of doing business reached their peak at this point.

May: Although sales of various woolen cloths were very strong, prices frequently fell. The main reason was still tight funds and an abundance of goods. The collapse of Ming-something, Mei-something, and both Chinese and foreign banks made businesses even more uneasy. New goods arrived cheaply, while old goods had high purchasing costs. Prices were chaotic due to the lack of a transition period. The price of Palais-something faltered particularly heavily. Rongtai Standard's old brand 15330 Constitutional Picture Durable Cloth also suddenly became chaotic because of a warehouse fire, which led to auction sales.

June: The weather was hot, and white goods for summer were all selling well in a timely manner. Striped white-somethings, patterned striped white direct yellow Palais-somethings, etc., sold particularly well. Yellow twill gauze, diagonal cloth, linen cloth, bunting cloth, beaded gauze, etc., also had smooth sales, but the price still fell. Only Japanese lower-grade white-somethings and thirty-six-inch.

July: Transactions were still good before the middle ten days of the month. Gray and white colors of yarn and wool-woven goods sold well. Transactions suddenly declined after the middle ten days of the month. Many in the industry sunned goods and took a summer break. This was a customary practice during the slack season over the years.

August: Autumn and winter woolen cloths of various kinds mostly opened for sale one after another. The prices quoted were all more favorable than the spring offerings in February. This was all due to the prevailing situation and environment, and not just a local phenomenon. Sichuan customers were the first to make purchases. Japanese woolen cloths were selling briskly, both in terms of arrivals and sales. British and German goods were severely impacted and had already occupied an important position. Following Rongtai, another well-known old business, Taihe, established a woolen cloth department.

September: The woolen cloth market showed great progress. Stores in this street all had a large volume of transactions. Foreign firms were shipping goods very busily. Postal parcel deliveries increased greatly. Unfortunately, prices continued to fall. Direct tribute cloth and riding breeches cloth were very favorable. Yarn plain thick cloth and Polish trading firms sold a lot of goods on the spot. Sellers generally held the principle of preferring to cut prices rather than extend credit.

October: Various woolen cloths sold well in a timely manner to domestic customers. Various men's and women's colored Western suit goods had large transactions every day. However, compared with previous years, sales decreased significantly because prices had fallen. From the 25th, woolen and quilted cloth prices saw a sudden contraction of prior orders, and customs duties and gold premiums soared, pushing up costs. As a result, many clamored for price increases. However, apart from overcoat cloth and yellow plain thick cloth, much of this was just a show of force. Silky bunting and horsehair satin also saw real sharp increases due to the soaring cost of rayon and yarn and wool raw materials. Eastern goods like thin floral cloth, medium-thick serge, and Polish overcoat cloth and yellow plain thick cloth showed better trends. Western goods like Halifax and high-striped floral cloth were particularly popular, with great demand from clothing tailors. Embroidered floral cloth with words on the selvage was fashionable for a time.

November: Cloth prices saw great changes. The government implemented the legal tender on the 4th, and people's minds were shaken. Woolen fabrics continued to rise in price. Sellers were unwilling to sell at prices lower than their original cost, while buyers bought only as needed. Polish goods saw the greatest increase. Japanese goods also saw sharp increases due to currency exchange rates. Domestic goods also reported price increases due to the high cost of raw materials. Transactions were limited because everyone needed legal tender, and sellers did not allow flexibility with checks (due to too many returned checks). As a result, there were only retail sales and few wholesale transactions. At the end of the month, the weather suddenly turned cold, and actual sales increased greatly. Plain thick cloth, medium-thick serge, riding breeches cloth, double-sided yellow camel down, "Ren" character woolen cloth, etc., continued to trade briskly (to be continued).

Shen Bao Children's Special

What Kind of Person Will I Be in the Future? 185

— Zhou Qingyan, Wujin County Dujiao Elementary School

I am a poor elementary school student. My home is near a towering factory (a weaving mill). My father works in this factory, and our family's livelihood depends entirely on him.

My father has a strong physique, bronze-colored skin, and large arms. Every day, before the east turns white, he gets up and rushes to the factory to start his day's work.

That factory is extremely large, with more than three thousand male and female workers. I have also visited every workshop. Dozens of machines are neatly arranged, moving in the same way: belts spinning rapidly, axles turning decisively, the sound of the machines rumbling, as if playing a great melody, making me feel relaxed and happy. My father said, "People who eat by their own labor are truly the noblest and most honorable people in the world. After you graduate next year, I will something you into the factory to work, because I believe that in the future world, those who do not work will not eat!" Hearing these words, I felt infinitely comfortable and honored, and I suddenly developed unlimited interest in "labor," "power," and "career." At the same time, the lighthouse for my future career direction has already revealed some faint rays of light.

Now, I am in the sixth grade, the last period of my schooling. Because after graduation, I will go to live in that active and lively world, and those capable arms will be used from then on. However, judging from my physique, current environment, and everything else, I can never become an ordinary worker. I must work hard. Because in this 20th century, inventors are not university students or overseas students, but workers. Edison was a newspaper boy when he was young, and Franklin was a printing worker in his childhood, but through various efforts, he eventually became a great inventor, benefiting mankind. I must work hard, I am determined to work hard! I vow to work hard! I will study the principles of machinery thoroughly and hope to become a great engineer.

Game Method to Enhance Children's Observation Skills 186

— Special

Now I will talk about a game method that is very beneficial and interesting for children. It can be tried anywhere, whether on a long train journey, in a quiet sit-down stroll by the seaside and in the forest, or in boredom while sitting at home on a rainy day. As long as there are three or five children, they can use this method to benefit the children and make them happy without feeling bored. This method is very simple. Just take some miscellaneous objects at hand, put them in front of the children, and tell them to pay attention and look at them. Then, immediately cover the objects with a large cloth or square scarf and ask each child to write down the names of the objects they can remember. Naturally, whoever writes the most correctly wins. This method can train children's memory. Because memory improves with training. At the same time, it can also enhance their observation skills, enabling them to pay attention to everything they see at any time. When we take children for a walk on the streets of the city, we can also play this game. For example, when passing a fruit store, you can ask the children to turn around and report the names of the various fruits they saw after a glance. If it is a grocery store, then you can ask him to report the various items displayed in the glass window. If you are strolling in the park, you can ask him to report what flowers, trees, birds, and houses he saw in the place he walked through a few minutes ago. In more detail, you can ask him to describe the shape, color, and type of each object separately. This method can be gradually extended to various scenes and various experiences in life.

Some schools are now using this method to improve students' memory and cultivate students' observation skills, and have achieved good results.

In the book "The Technique of Thinking" by Nietz, there is a quote from the son of the famous painter Carini, who said: "My father often took me for a walk in the countryside. When we encountered a beautiful scene, we would stop and observe it quietly for a few minutes. Then we would both turn around and try to recall the characteristics of the beautiful scene that were imprinted in our minds during that moment of observation." He also said: "My father's observation and memory are very strong. He often remembers the points that ordinary people cannot observe even after a few months, without any errors." This characteristic is not innate, nor can it be obtained in one day. It all depends on practicing observation skills in peacetime. Over time, it becomes a habit. All the beautiful natural landscapes and the various interesting points around us can be deeply imprinted in our minds after seeing them. As a result, experience can become richer day by day, and studies can be easily successful. Conversely, if there is a lack of such practice, the various things seen are like clouds passing before the eyes, and cannot be imprinted in the mind at all. Because things seen by chance are most easily overlooked and something. The so-called "absent-mindedness, seeing but not seeing, hearing but not something." Many scholars in the world have become famous by using their daily experience in observing things. Therefore, we should train children's memory and observation skills from an early age.

###

—

Isn't the weather these days very cold? Ah! Children! Do you have a stove at home? Alas! Don't you often see in the newspaper every year that a family has been poisoned by gas? Do you know why they died? I'm afraid you may not be able to answer! This is because of the lack of knowledge about gas. Now, I'll take this opportunity to talk to everyone about it.

The main cause of death is mostly because the stove does not have a pipe, and the gas has no way to escape. As a result, the gas combines with oxygen to become carbon dioxide. Also, because the oxygen in the room is limited, and the air exhaled by people is also dead air, the continued production of gas does not have oxygen to combine with, and the room is filled with carbon monoxide, but its nature is poisonous, and it has solidified. Blood loses its blood characteristics and its instinct, and naturally will not circulate, and people will die.

Children! If you encounter a poisoned person, you should drag the poisoned person to an open space, and then use artificial respiration to revive him. This is also a meritorious thing. Also, the room where the stove is burning must feel very dry. Then, you only need to put a pot of water on the stove, and the pot will have water vapor, which will be released continuously to regulate the humidity, which is very hygienic. Finally, I hope that the children can explain the knowledge about gas to their neighbors, so that they all know the horror of gas poisoning and the methods of rescue.

Dear children:

At this time when the country is in trouble, I know that you will definitely work harder to study, and I also know that you may be writing a diary every day. Now I want to talk to you about the benefits and methods of writing a diary.

What should I record in my diary? Many children always say when writing a diary, what should I record? Dear children! Do you have this feeling that there is nothing to write about? The Three-Legged Ostrich 191

— Gulang

One day, Ah Xi came back from school and said to his mother:

"Mom? I got first place on the natural science exam":

Mom asked happily:

"Ah Xi! Really? What question did the teacher ask you? Tell me quickly":

Ah Xi said:

"The question the teacher asked me was how many legs does an ostrich have, and I said it has three legs."

Mom said:

"No, an ostrich has two legs, how could you get first place?"

Ah Xi said: "No, I'm not lying. There are ten people in our class, and nine of them said that an ostrich has four legs. The teacher said I was closer, so I got first place!"

The Tale of the Righteous Dog (4) 192

— Xinqing

He looked at Bo Deshi and stopped in surprise. He moved aside, knelt down in the viewing grass and reeds by the ditch, with a look of pity in his eyes, focused on Bo Deshi's body.

With him was a yellow-haired, black-eyed child with cheeks like roses, who had not been born for a few years. He ran busily in the chest-high dwarf trees, talking. After a while, he stopped and carefully looked at the poor big dog lying still.

This was their first meeting! Little Nanluo and Bo Deshi.

The result of this day was that Old Dashifei spent a lot of effort to drag the poor dog to his own small house area and carefully took care of it. It didn't have any serious injuries, just because it was thirsty, tired, and exposed to the summer heat, its head was dizzy, and it really couldn't bear it. Now, after resting in a cool place, it regained its original strength and health. It finally stood up on its four powerful legs.

In the first few weeks, it felt weak and helpless, close to death; but it didn't hear a harsh word all day, and no whips or sticks touched its body. All it heard was the child's pitying soft voice, and all it felt was the old man's comforting stroking.

During its illness, this lonely old man and that happy child were its most sincere caregivers.

It occupied a corner in this small house, with a pile of hay for its something bed; they always listened to its breathing sound very earnestly in the dark, knowing that it was still alive; when it regained some strength and was able to make a discontinuous bark, they laughed happily, even to the point of crying with joy, because they knew it had recovered; Little Nanluo was happy as if something. He picked many small chrysanthemums and made a wreath to put around its neck and kissed its bright red lips.

So Bo Deshi became lively again, still strong and powerful as before; in its pair of hot big eyes, there was a very surprised look, how come no one beat it or scolded it now; it felt a great love in its heart, which it had never had before.

Children's Science Lecture: Currency 193

— Linyin

After Shennong established the method of "trading at noon", there were times and places for transactions in society. However, at that time, the people still had a problem. They felt that it was inconvenient to exchange goods for goods, and the prices of goods were high and low, so some suffered losses and some got bargains in the exchange. Therefore, Shennong also thought of a kind of intermediate product of trade to replace the value of goods. At that time, shells and leather (Figure 1) were used, which is the origin of currency.

Later, everyone felt that shells and leather were inconvenient, so they came up with the idea of using metal to cast currency. This was the evolution of currency. Some were knife-shaped, some were square with round holes in the middle, and some looked like bells. (Figure 2) From the time of the Yellow Emperor, it was used until the Han Dynasty.

After many improvements, the value of the currency itself was used to determine the price represented by the currency, such as small coins cast from copper, small change cast from silver, and silver dollars, which were of high value. (Figure 3) And the use value of various currencies is specified. My country uses silver dollars as the main body, called the silver standard, like the United Kingdom uses gold pounds as the main body, called the gold standard.

However, metal currency also has a disadvantage. Its weight is too heavy and it is inconvenient to carry. If the amount of money going in and out is large, it takes a lot of time to count. Therefore, paper money was invented later, commonly known as banknotes. (Figure 3) This kind of money is light and easy to collect, and it is the most convenient type of currency.

Now, in order to unify the monetary system and relieve finance, the government has stipulated that the paper money of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications is legal currency. That is to say, the banknotes of these three banks are currencies recognized and used by the country, and the use of silver dollars has been prohibited. And the exchange of unified currency is that each small silver dollar is worth 250 copper coins, and one yuan of legal currency can be exchanged for 12 small silver dollars, or 3,000 copper coins. In this way, the use of currency something is more something.
