Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Small-Scale Monographs

The Genesis and Function of Buddhism 194

— Jingzai

Buddhism is a kind of religious thought that opposed Brahmanism, but it is not entirely unrelated to Brahmanism. Furthermore, we must observe it from the perspective of the changes in Indian social group relations to understand its genesis and the function of its doctrines. Around 1000 BC, it was the era of the Aryan conquest of India. The great Indian epics, the Mahabharata with its 100,000 verses and the Ramayana with its 24,000 verses, record the historical events of this period of war. Mr. Lü in his "Brief History of Indian Buddhism" said that at the beginning of the Aryan conquest of India, a naturalistic religion that worshipped natural objects emerged, and the Brahmins were the priests who created Brahmanism. The Brahmins also "sang praises of the grandeur of celestial phenomena and earthly instruments with utmost detail. The spirits they worshipped initially took the forms of natural objects but gradually came to believe that they possessed moral qualities, capable of bestowing rewards and punishments. At the same time, they cultivated philosophical thought." Thus, Brahmanism truly originated from primitive natural fetishism, and the source of the so-called four Vedas’ doctrines also stemmed from this. However, after the Aryan people conquered the indigenous people of India, they themselves became the ruling aristocracy, so the religion they believed in gradually became the religion of the ruling class. Furthermore, due to their position of dominance and widespread development, the priests who believed and performed sacrifices naturally became a special class, transforming into the highest rulers. However, precisely because the Aryans and Brahmin priests became the rulers, they no longer needed to engage in outward warfare and killing as they did when they first invaded India. They only sought to maintain their rule and current status, and even only pursued a life of comfort and spiritual salvation and liberation. Therefore, Brahmanism gradually changed its religious thought, transforming its religious doctrines from natural fetishism to research that "became increasingly lofty and profound," "combining the nature of philosophy and religion," thinking to "exhaust the mysteries of the universe and escape the realm of birth and death," "establishing profound theories." Some leaned toward contemplative thought, while others were earnest in the path of liberation and became hermits.

However, since the Aryan people ruled India as foreigners and became the highest ruling aristocracy, and the priests who believed in their religion also became the highest rulers, the indigenous aristocrats of India inevitably became the ruled, occupying an inferior position. The Indian society at that time was divided into four classes. The Aryan aristocrats and Brahmin priests naturally occupied the highest ruling position and were satisfied with the status quo. However, the indigenous people of India, from aristocrats to slaves, and even the lower strata of Aryan and Brahmin society, were all dissatisfied with the status quo and opposed it. A complex essence of group struggle naturally existed here, and anti-Brahmanism thus became a widespread ideology. The rise of Buddhist doctrines represented this anti-Brahmanism trend. This movement was participated in, and even led by, the ruled aristocracy. Therefore, Shakyamuni was born into the Shakya clan, a non-Aryan group in India, and his position was that of a king's prince within that clan. This proves that some aristocrats were often resisters against the rulers. However, at that time, the social economy of India was based on a slave society. On the one hand, the resistance of the slave groups themselves could not embark on a path of organized resistance activities. On the other hand, even under the leadership of the aristocracy, they could not trust them to rise up and engage in practical resistance, so as to shake their own position. Therefore, that kind of passive resistance only in consciousness was most suited to their needs, and the doctrines of Buddhism took this kind of intention as their central thought.

Once we understand the group relations and group psychology of India at the time of the rise of Buddhism, the reasons for the rise of the Buddhist movement will naturally be clear. At the same time, we can also understand the true meaning and function of its doctrines. Buddhist doctrine recognizes that everything is impermanent, and the real world is suffering.

Page 20

Page 21

The reason why the real world is suffering is because of impermanence, because impermanence means constant change, and constant change means suffering. In terms of human life, birth, aging, sickness, and death are changes, so it considers birth, aging, sickness, and death as suffering. Transcending birth, aging, sickness, and death is the liberation from suffering, that is, transcending change and being able to not experience any change is liberation. This kind of thought that is hostile to change, that considers change as suffering, is honestly the fear and lament of the aristocracy themselves. Because they are attached to their old positions, they realize that they were once rulers, but now they are oppressed, so they are very sad about the deterioration of their positions and want to obtain something constant and unchanging. Naturally, they will be hostile to this change and impermanence, and consider it as suffering. In their view, change is emptiness, because something that exists becomes nothing when it changes. Their original superiority becomes non-superior, and everything in the past is lost in the midst of change, so their philosophy recognizes that changing things are illusion and emptiness. All the myriad things in reality are changing, so all things are empty. The Four Great Elements are empty is their ultimate epistemological philosophy. They use this to deny the material world, and consider everything that is fragrant, flavorful, tangible, and perceptible to be empty. Although they take everything as emptiness as the basis of their knowledge, they are not satisfied with this emptiness. Emptiness arises from change, so they have to seek something unchanging and eternal to fill their emptiness. Thus, they attribute the external world entirely to consciousness. Things are formed by consciousness, and the changing world is also formed by consciousness. If we want to forget all the changes in the external world, and not be tainted or suffer from the changing external world, then we can only achieve this by not focusing on it, by realizing that the unchanging Suchness. In this way, if we eliminate material desires and attachment to the real world, and sweep away external conditions and worldly knowledge to clarify the mind and see its nature, then we can obtain liberation, which is also their method of escaping suffering. Buddhist practice takes this as its purpose, so its asceticism is otherworldly.

However, the above-mentioned Buddhist doctrines are the highest orthodox doctrines of the Yogacara school of Mahayana Buddhism, while the doctrines of Hinayana remain within the cycle of cause and effect, birth, death, and reincarnation. People with profound Buddhist thought generally despise it. In fact, in our view, although Mahayana Buddhism is the authentic and original Buddhism, it is the doctrine of the aristocrats. Because although they express opposition to the alteration of their old positions, they also oppose continued edification, and take transcending the changing world to reach the Suchness of enlightened minds as liberation. But this is precisely what people who still have food to eat and blessings to enjoy do, and they are even more unwilling to accept the consequences of cause and effect and reincarnation, nor are they willing to die old and sick, because they do not want to suffer the consequences of being an exploiter in the next life, nor do they want their positions to deteriorate again in reincarnation. As for the Hinayana school, it is different. Although its negative otherworldly thought still originates from Buddhism and is subject to the anesthesia and deception of the aristocracy, the aristocrats' doctrines have changed in their hands. Because they hope that by cultivating good causes in this life, they can be reincarnated into the upper class in the next life and obtain good results. Therefore, Mahayana and Hinayana can be said to express different ideals of groups, containing the meaning of group opposition within them.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Introducing "Healthy World" 195

— Quanqing

Published by Kangjian Shijie She, No. 14, Lane 214, Tongfu Road, this city. The price per issue is five cents, and the annual subscription for twelve issues is fifty cents.

In our several consecutive "magazine years," quite a few magazines have indeed appeared; and, in the midst of these, the number of general comprehensive magazines and special specialized magazines has been increasing. However, among these various magazines, if you want to find a practical, easy-to-understand publication about our health, then I have no other publication to recommend to you that better suits your wishes than the recently published "Healthy World."

In the introductory remarks of "Healthy World," the six major missions of this publication are expressed: Promote the true meaning of health; Research the science of health; Advocate health movements; Introduce health news; Disseminate medical knowledge; Realize a happy life. According to the contents of the first and second issues of this publication, it has indeed implemented many of the above-mentioned major missions. Regarding promoting the true meaning of health and methods of health, the inaugural issue contains Kangjian Qifu's "From the Desire for Survival to Health and National Destiny," Zhinan's "Health Education and Life," Huang Jiping's "Mr. Ge Gongzhen's Pre-Mortem Hygiene Talk," and the second issue contains Yi Mei's "Mr. Li Hefei's Health Talk," Mr. Zhou Yimin's "Several Points to Pay Attention to Regarding Health"... Regarding women's and children's health, the inaugural issue contains Shi Dong's "Health and Women," Letian Qifu's "Children's Healthy Life," Yuan Wen's "Several Practical Key Points on Children's Hygiene," and the second issue contains Chu Yao's "Methods for Producing Excessive Breast Milk." These articles are all very practical, and anyone who reads them can gain many benefits. Regarding physical education, there is Zhi Zhi's "Ten Tennis Aces" (second issue)... etc. However, I think the best part of this publication, the most beneficial part for general readers, is still the "Medical Spring and Autumn" column, and a few more words need to be said about this here.

As Fangbian Jun pointed out in "Respectfully Informing Patients" (inaugural issue) and "Again Informing Patients" (second issue), many medical publications in the country are "speaking true prescriptions but selling fake medicines," are "setting traps" to "deceive patients out of their money," and are of a low-grade advertising nature. These things are not only useless to the general reader, especially patients, but also harmful. The "Medical Spring and Autumn" column of "Healthy World" is absolutely different from this type of medical publication. The articles here do not promote individuals, nor do they advertise medicines that sound good but are actually not very effective. They all study various pathologies scientifically and objectively, explain the prevention and treatment of various diseases, and examine the properties of certain foods related to our health and explain their uses. Moreover, these articles are all highly relevant to our actual lives and are of practical use to us. For example, Dr. Zhang Jianqing's "Milk and Health" in the inaugural issue explains the quality of milk and how to eat it in a very practical way; also, such as Yu Chen's "Colds and Influenza" (inaugural issue), Wu Hongyou's "Chatting about Diphtheria," Zhang Jianqing's "Talking about Contraception," and Gu Baoluo's "Drug-Free Therapy for Neurasthenia" (the above three articles are published in the second issue) are all very scientific and practical things. If our families and ourselves inevitably encounter illnesses, and if we need to eat some tonics to maintain our health, then often browsing such a "Healthy World," especially its "Medical Spring and Autumn" column, is indeed very beneficial, because from this we can obtain a lot of useful medical and health knowledge.

In addition, the articles in "Healthy World" are also very easy to understand; anyone, as long as they are literate, can understand them. In this regard, it can also be said that this publication is different from the completely rigid things that generally only talk about academic theory.

Celebrity Interview Records

Mr. Yu Qiaqing's Interview Record 196

— Kans

There is an American called "Shipping King" Dollar, whose ships are said to be all over the world, and commercial ships with Dollar Company flags can be seen on any route. In the eyes of ordinary people, this Mr. Dollar is certainly considered a remarkable figure. However, in a country with developed capital and so easily producing "Kings," becoming a "Shipping King" seems much easier than in China. Although China's shipping industry has nearly a hundred years of history, it still seems to be in its infancy due to various reasons. It is conceivable how difficult it would be to create a "Shipping King" in this immature industry. However, despite the immaturity of China's entire shipping administration, there are still individuals who have achieved success. For example, Mr. Yu Qiaqing is an excellent role model in the shipping industry.

Mr. Yu is from Longshan, Zhenhai. At the age of fifteen, he came to Shanghai from his hometown to pursue a career in commerce, diligently working for fifty-four years. In the twentieth year of the Republic of China, prominent figures in Shanghai held a fiftieth anniversary celebration for him to commemorate this extraordinary person. I have long admired Mr. Yu, but I have not had the opportunity to learn from him. This time, thanks to the introduction of Mr. Xu, the editor of a certain journal, through family connections, I was able to have a pleasant one-hour conversation with this celebrity in the shipping industry.

It was a Monday afternoon when I entered the general manager's office of the Sanbei Company. Mr. Yu was focused on handling his daily affairs. After I handed him my letter of introduction, he courteously invited me to sit down.

He is sixty-nine years old this year, and should be an old man in his twilight years, but looking at his radiant, square-shaped face and bright, piercing eyes, he still seems to be in his prime. His tone of voice has not changed his native accent (Zhenjiang accent) despite living in Shanghai for fifty years, but due to his age, it seems even more aged.

"Mr. Yu, you must be very busy with official matters? If you have time, I would like to ask you to tell me about your past experiences. I believe you have a lot of experiences that can serve as a model for young people." I explained my purpose.

"I'm just doing some routine work every day, so I can't say I'm that busy. But asking me to tell you about my past experiences as a model for young people, I don't think there's any good material worth providing you!"

"Don't be modest, Mr. Yu! I heard that your current position is entirely due to your struggle in difficult circumstances. In this process, there must be a lot of valuable material. It is said that you used to learn business in a paint shop, is that true?"

"Yes." His tone was as firm as cutting nails. Then, he closed one eye and deeply recalled, "That was more than fifty years ago. The paint shop where I was an apprentice was called Ruikang, and it was opened by Mr. Xi Runru. At that time, the scale was very small, with a capital of only eight hundred taels. The shop used only three 'Chaofeng' (shop assistants). Later, when I joined, there were a total of four people. In addition to doing what an ordinary apprentice should do, I also served as a street runner..."

I waited for him to rest for a moment and then asked, "Why were you so interested in the paint industry back then?"

"When I came from my hometown, I originally planned to go to a small money shop in Nanshi Dawang Temple to learn about money matters. However, because another fellow villager, Mr. So-and-so, came with me, and he couldn't wait for long after arriving in Shanghai due to the circumstances at the time, Mr. Yu Jiu, a member of our clan who brought us to Shanghai, introduced him to the small money shop first. I only joined Ruikang Paint Shop later." A pleasant smile spread across his radiant face, and he tightened his hands further into his sleeves.

"It is said that the manager of the shop dreamed of a barefoot God of Wealth the night before you joined Ruikang. The next day, when you joined the shop, it was raining heavily, and coincidentally, you had taken off your shoes and socks. The manager was overjoyed when he saw it. Is this also true?"

"That was also a coincidence," he said, smiling, "But it was indeed raining heavily on the day I joined the shop, and the only pair of new shoes I had just put on my feet. At the time, I really felt sorry for them, so I took them off along with my socks. If transportation in Shanghai were as convenient as it is now, perhaps there wouldn't be such far-fetched stories."

"However, it is said that you earned more than 20,000 taels in the year you joined the shop. I think even if that kind of story is a 'far-fetched statement,' it doesn't seem to be without reason, right?"

"No!" He leaned back in his chair, seeming slightly displeased with my words, and then said, "That kind of legend is just the superstitious thinking of old people. If business makes money, it is attributed to the gods; if it fails, they complain about their fate. In modern commerce, we must never have this kind of thinking. The success or failure of a business has its inherent causes and objective environment, and it is definitely not something that can be achieved by accidental acquisition or seeking the protection of the gods. The year I joined the shop was when the paint business had great potential, but some people didn't see this point. So, after I was assigned to be a street runner shortly after joining the shop, I tried my best to work hard in my duties. Of course! There is no easy theorem that one must cultivate to reap the rewards, so at the end of that year, the result of my hard work was a profit of more than 20,000 taels of silver." He flashed two fingers in the air and then inserted them back into his sleeves.

"In that year, the shop should have given you a great reward for your hard work, right?" I said with a smile.

"You young people always like to think about it from this perspective. However, according to the old rules of the shops at the time, apprentices usually only received twelve yuan for shoes and socks at the end of the year. That year, because I earned more than 20,000 taels, the shop was particularly polite to me and added forty yuan for shoes and socks. This was indeed an unprecedented example in the business community at the time." He shook four fingers at me like a fan, showing a very satisfied look with the situation at the time.

"You probably stayed at Ruikang for several years, right?"

"More than ten years. In the second year there, a paint shop called Santai wanted to hire me as a 'Chaofeng'先生, but Mr. Xi didn't want me to leave, so he voluntarily gave up two shares of Ruikang to me. At the time, I couldn't bear to leave Ruikang myself, so I pooled together two hundred taels of silver to join the shares. From then on, Ruikang's business became more and more prosperous day by day, earning more and more money year by year. At this time, I was both a shareholder and an employee. Every year, I always got a little profit, and I also had a small reputation in society. So, I used the money I earned in society to give back to society. For all social undertakings, as long as my ability and financial resources could reach, I always tried my best to support them."

"When did you give up the paint business?"

"I ran the paint business for twelve years. At that time, I was only twenty-seven years old. Not long after, I accepted the invitation of Roullin & Company to serve as a comprador. I also worked there for nine years before switching to Daosheng Bank. Because of many reasons, I only worked at Daosheng for one year, and then joined the Netherlands Bank as a comprador again. This time was the longest period I served in the financial industry, almost thirty years."

"Mr. Yu, the number of years you've worked is much older than my age! Did you do other businesses during such a long period? When did you start in the shipping industry?"

"Haha!" He pondered for a moment, smiling, "Speaking of this, it's also a matter of decades ago. My motivation for engaging in the shipping industry was also driven by the circumstances at the time. Because in the late Guangxu years, the number of fellow villagers traveling between Shanghai and Ningbo for business increased day by day. At that time, only two ships, Taikoo's 'Beijing' and China Merchants Bureau's 'Jiangtian,' were sailing on the Shanghai-Ningbo route, which was quite in short supply. The unified ticket price was more expensive than other routes, and the general fellow villagers were suffering. Not long after, the French-organized Eastern Company's 'Lida' ship joined the route, wanting to seize the passenger transport of Taikoo and China Merchants. As a result, Taikoo and China Merchants jointly lowered the price to absorb passengers, and the ticket price fell from one yuan to five corners. This situation lasted only one year. The three companies resumed 'reconciliation' and restored the ticket price to the original amount of one yuan, making the general fellow villagers feel the pain of exploitation again. Seeing this situation, I contacted the authorities of the three companies, requesting that the ticket price for the steerage cabin should never exceed five corners, otherwise, the Ningbo people would start their own company and purchase ships to run. However, the result of running back and forth was still not getting the sympathy of the three companies. From this, I deeply felt that foreign capitalists only absorbed profits from China as much as possible, and there was absolutely no trace of morality to speak of. If we want to talk to them, we have to strengthen our own strength first. After this stimulation, I was determined to organize a Ning Shao Company. However, the most important tool for running a shipping company is the wharf. Without a wharf, it is like the foot of a person suffering from hemiplegia, with only the appearance, but in reality, it is of no use at all. However, at that time, the better sections along the Huangpu River were 'snapped up' by foreign companies, and the wharf of the Ning Shao Company became a very important issue. Later, there was no way, so I had to rent the Dongyang Company wharf east of the Waibaidu Bridge from the Japanese, but it was not successful. Then, I rented the wharf south of Waiyangjing Bridge, opposite the French Consulate, from 'Santetang,' but it was also defeated. Finally, I petitioned the Governor-General of Liangjiang in Nanjing and the Ministry of Agriculture, Industry and Commerce in Beijing, and asked Mr. Zhang Jian from Nantong for help, which solved this important problem. When the Ning Shao Company started business, it first followed the principle of only selling the steerage cabin ticket price for five corners. The general fellow villagers, seeing that it was a self-run shipping industry and the ticket price was low, rushed to take the Ning Shao ships. This aroused the jealousy of the three companies, so they lowered the ticket price from one yuan to two corners, wanting to use the strength of large capital to defeat the Ning Shao Company. However, the unity of us Ningbo people is not bad. When the general fellow villagers saw this situation, everyone was very enthusiastic to help and donated cash to organize a Shipping Industry Maintenance Association. The association sold tickets to the outside world at a uniform price of three corners, and the association subsidized the company for the insufficient amount, which cost tens of thousands of yuan. From then on, the unity of the Chinese nation was noticed by foreigners."

"Sanbei Company was established after the Ning Shao Company, right?"

"No!" He looked at the clock on the wall and then said, "First there was Sanbei, then there was Ning Shao. The reason for running the Sanbei Company was to facilitate the transportation of Longshan. Also, because Longshan is located in the northern township of Zhenhai, Cixi, and Yuyao, there is the name of this Sanbei Company. Initially, there were only three ships sailing, Zhenbei, Cibei, and Yaobei; Cibei Yaobei traveled to Chuanshan, Zhoushan, and Shenjiamen, while Zhenbei sailed on the Yongjiang River and connected to the Shanghai-Ningbo line. At that time, the scale of Sanbei Company was very small, with a capital of only 200,000 yuan, and all the equipment was very simple. However, because Longshan produced a lot of cotton and beans, the cargo transportation was very considerable. In the early years of the Republic of China, the British-owned Hongan Shipping Company was taken over. At this time, I had the idea of recovering navigation rights. Hongan has two ships, 'Changan' and 'Dexing,' and wharves and warehouses in Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Jiujiang, and Hankou. After I took over, because there were still many British shareholders, doing things was inevitably restricted by them, so in the fourth year of the Republic of China, I raised one million capital to buy out the equity of the British and changed the company name to Hongan Commercial Shipping Company. At one time, the two ships 'Changan' and 'Dexing' and the wharves and warehouses in various places were replaced with the flags of Chinese merchant ships. At the same time, Sanbei Company also added branches in various ports. From then on, I personally became a strong enemy of Jardine Matheson and Taikoo in shipping.

"In the seventh year of the Republic of China, the capital of Sanbei Company was increased by 3 million yuan, and two new 3,000-ton ocean-going ships were added to sail on the North and South Ocean routes. Because at this time, the navigation rights of the coastal ports were still in the hands of foreigners, if we don't find a way to resist, in the future, even the territorial waters will be given away together. Sanbei Company was originally a very small company, but after my personal and many colleagues' continuous efforts, the nerves of a group of foreign shipping companies who were 'ignorant of their own limitations' had to be shaken, and they no longer dared to treat Sanbei Company as carelessly as before. Now Sanbei has a total of 29 ships. Today, when the inland navigation rights have been cancelled, it is the time when our country's shipping industry should work hard!"

"Mr. Yu can be considered a 'Shipping King' in China's shipping industry!"

"I don't dare to be complacent," he waved his hands at me repeatedly. "But we still have to try our best to expand the established business, which is what an entrepreneur should do."

"Yes, your views are precisely the proverbs that young students should admire. Mr. Yu, is your personal life still the same as before?" I felt that there were too many things to ask about his past career, so I turned the question to his personal life here.

"The current lifestyle has not changed much from the past. Every day I leave home at 9:00 am and go to a few places I should go to first. At about 11:00 am, I come to Sanbei Company to work. I like to ask about everything in the company, no matter how big or small, but therefore, some people who don't understand me think I am a 'dictator.' In fact, this is just a habit that has been developed over decades of hard work in social undertakings. For example, when things are busy, I even have to eat lunch outside casually to finish things. I work in the afternoon until 8:00 pm before I can go back. If there are social events, I have no way of knowing what time I can go back."

"Then you can simply be said to be living for society. I heard that you are still very frugal even now. Sometimes when you come to the company, you are reluctant to take the elevator. Isn't that a bit too harsh!"

"I don't think it's too harsh. Sometimes walking more is also very comfortable. Fortunately, my feet are still healthy, and I don't feel tired even walking from the bottom to the third floor. In the eyes of modern young people, this kind of life is bound to be considered too frugal, but I am from the heart and it has no effect. When I went back at that time, if I happened to not have a car, I would spend a dozen coppers to take a rickshaw. I never wanted to ask my servants to prepare it for me, because the price of the car they called was always several coppers more expensive than the one I called myself."

"Looking at it this way, Mr. Yu is simply an economist....”

"I'm not an economist, but not wasting money is also my belief..."

Celebrity Biography

French Automobile King Citroen 197

— Xiaotian

Speaking of automobile kings, people will mention Ford, but in fact, André Citroën was also once called the automobile king along with Ford. Ten years ago, in 1925, Citroën's car achieved the record for the highest speed, making the progress of French automobile manufacturing technology known to the world. At that time, in Paris, in France, congratulations and praises for Citroën could be seen almost everywhere, and conversations about him could be heard everywhere! At the same time, he, who was called the King of Paris, was of course very happy, dreaming that every citizen of Paris would buy a Citroën car from him.

The Citroën car appeared during the Great War. Compared with the original Loro car, it was the lightest, most fashionable, and most popular at that time, so after the end of the Great War, Citroën's wealth was calculated in millions. In many places, he set up many new factories. He did not hesitate to spend tens of millions of gold on advertising expenses to compete in business. His momentum was so great at the time that it can be said to have alarmed all of Europe. His dominant power was not only manifested in the European market, but also extended to Asia and Africa. The so-called Citroën car can be said to have galloped around the world.

Citroën was born in 1878, his parents

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

His name was still little known, but with the development of the Great War, his business became increasingly prosperous. The name of the so-called genius of the economic world, the King of Paris, was also spread everywhere.

He was originally an engineer. After returning from a trip to the United States in 1912, he worked hard to improve and expand his factory, so that he could produce hundreds of cars per month. The Great War continued to develop, and the sound of artillery fire was heard all over the world, which gave him an opportunity to make a fortune. In fact, in the four years of the Great War, his business had developed amazingly. By 1919, his unique cars could be seen everywhere. In 1925, his reputation was comparable to that of automobile king Ford.

In today's world, there will naturally be opportunities for sudden wealth, but it is also very easy to　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　Opportunity made a fortune and became an automobile king, but in the recent economic panic, in the ruthless business competition of capitalism, his business also suffered the fate of decline, collapse, and bankruptcy.

Ten years ago, on a tall advertising tower in the Paris night sky, the words Citroen lit up with electric lights, which became one of the gorgeous night scenes of Paris and was known to all Parisians. But now? The bright electric words in the night sky are only in people's memories. The newspaper published the news of the collapse of Citroën Company. The factory of the so-called automobile king Citroën has been managed by his creditors, and the famous he has finally become bankrupt and died!

Even so, Citroën's contribution to society is still great, and his spirit of struggle in his career is still worth emulating.

Miscellaneous Works

Small Steamboat 198

— Ka

The shadow of my hometown has long been faded in my dreams. For this declining year, the heart of a wanderer is inexplicably troubled again. Indeed, years of wandering have made me feel the fatigue of traveling. So, I also miss my home in my consciousness.

As the iron wheels rumbled forward on the tracks, I sat silently among the countless passengers in the carriage.

The atmosphere of the city completely fell behind the train. The sparse branches outside the window rushed backward. The sunlight was vaguely sprinkled on the gray-brown soil. The train passed through the forest, and a flock of chirping sparrows was startled in the tranquil jungle.

How much I miss these familiar and unfamiliar scenes!

There is no shortage of lively conversations in the car, talking about the decline of the market, which stores in Shanghai have closed down, and also talking about a Miss So-and-so's swimming to save the country.

After getting off the train, I still have to take a two-mao small ferry and a four-mao rickshaw to get home. Because it is closer to my hometown, there are a few familiar villagers on the small ferry. They still mention that the new small steamboat has sailed in Louzhen, which I used to see four years ago, and the rickshaw can be replaced by the small steamboat. Even such a small place is gradually approaching science.

When the ferry arrived at the dock, I really wanted to take the newly sailed small steamboat, and my heart was dominated by a kind of novelty desire.

The dock was as crowded as before with a group of laborers, shouting, waving, and competing for customers' luggage.

"Two mao to Louzhen! Two mao! Only two mao!" A clear voice entered my ears.

"Mr. So-and-so hasn't returned to his hometown for a long time!"

It turned out that Ajiang was still doing his rickshaw pulling career. Because of his warm greetings, my desire to take the small steamboat changed again, and I blindly stepped on Ajiang's rickshaw.

Ajiang is old, and his back seems to be very hunched.

Most of the thirty or forty passengers on the ferry transferred to the small steamboat. Only four people took the rickshaw, including me. Most of the rickshaw pullers were still standing at the dock, staring blankly at the small steamboat rushing away. Our four rickshaws passed through the bustling town and moved forward in a vast green field.

I asked Ajiang, "Has Louzhen changed anything?"

"It's still the same old way, except that East Street was burned down in a fire. Besides, we rickshaw pullers are afraid that we will have no food to eat soon."

"How come? Aren't you still pulling rickshaws?"

"Oh, sir, don't you know? With the small steamboat, we won't have rickshaws!" He coughed and choked, paused, and said again, "We have a big price cut, two mao to Louzhen, but the guests still take the one-mao-five steamboat. We also have to go to Louzhen for one mao five, and the car pull is used as a steamboat!"

My heart was immediately pressed down by the heavy pain of lead. A magnificent scene of the struggle between human power and machines unfolded before me.

The earth mounds undulated. The steamboat also turned into the Hengli River in front. A wisp of black smoke curled into the air from the water, and it called out "Gua—Gua—" twice. In the lonely sky, there was still only the sound of the rattling of the rickshaws.

"Damn it, the heart of the old man, Li, is as black as charcoal. He rents cars to us on one hand..."

He suddenly stopped, but undoubtedly, he was full of anger.

"What's wrong?" I asked.

"Hmph, we rented cars from him, and he went to drive a small steamboat. Damn it, the car rent can't be reduced by a penny."

Ajiang was completely emotional, and he coughed and choked even more.

The rickshaw arrived at the door of my house. I took out four mao of small silver coins for this man with a sweaty head. He seemed surprised by my behavior. He probably thought that the price of four mao had become a redundant number under the current situation.

The white silver coin stayed in his palm for thirty seconds before he hunched his back, said a solemn thank you, and left.

It was already late, and black fog had shrouded the low eaves.

Book and Newspaper Chronicles

Review of "A History of China" 199

— Hua Xing

— Published by the Cultural Society in front of Hepingmen, Beiping. Four volumes, priced at $8.20 —

For the past several thousand years, Chinese history has been recorded by scholars employed by the imperial court, according to the imperial court's wishes. Therefore, even if you read all of the Twenty-Four Histories, Twenty-Five Histories, all of the historical books of past China, all that you can see are the words and deeds of emperors and nobles, the accomplishments of wise rulers and loyal ministers, and the crimes of rebellious officials and traitors. As for the economic conditions of each era, the state of social life, and the social causes of various historical events, those are nowhere to be found. The most interesting thing in all of this is the "praise and blame" attitude of the "historians;" this is the so-called "the victor is king, the loser is bandit" attitude. Under this attitude, actions such as "Tang banishing Jie," "King Wu attacking Zhou," Wang Mang destroying the Western Han, the Cao family usurping the throne, Li Yuan destroying the Sui, and even Huang Chao raising an army, although fundamentally similar in nature, are treated differently under the "praise and blame" of those "historians." The successful ones, whose power lasted longer, are praised as righteous armies, removing harm for the people, even fabricating myths, calling them "ordained by Heaven." Otherwise, they are treacherous officials usurping the throne and murdering the ruler, or bandits plotting rebellion. Therefore, even now, we cannot rely on existing historical materials to scientifically and systematically organize a true history of China.

Of course, in the current situation, anyone who can scientifically and systematically organize a history of China would be making a great contribution. But if someone still follows the methods of those "historiographers" of the past autocratic era, adopting the "the victor is king, the loser is bandit" attitude of "praise and blame," and copies a history of China from the "official histories," then this undertaking is not only equivalent to doing nothing at all, but also reveals the vulgarity of the person doing it, lacking any new historical perspective. However, such a vulgar person doing such a thing already exists: Mr. Wang Tongling. His "History of China" is copied from the so-called "official histories."

It sounds a bit scary, but Mr. Wang Tongling's "History of China" consists of four massive volumes, over two thousand pages, with at least a million words. But if you consider that the "official histories" of all Chinese dynasties are readily available, and copying all the official histories of the dynasties of the past several thousand years into one pile to copy, then compiling a large book of several million words probably wouldn't be that difficult. However, leaving that aside, let's talk more specifically about the content of Mr. Wang's "History of China."

In the "General Principles" of the "History of China," there is a clause that says: "The style of this compilation is a general history, paying the most attention to the rise and fall of the nation and the prosperity and demise of the country. All matters concerning rise, fall, prosperity, and demise are described in detail, with their causes and results, to serve as a lesson for the present and future generations." From this, it seems that the compiler of this book is quite nationalistic. But when we open the first page of the book, what the compiler uses to replace the first preface is a short essay on Chinese history written by a certain doctor from a certain country. After recounting the course of past Chinese history from his own standpoint, the author made the following conclusion: "For the sake of China, uniting with the country geographically closest and the nation culturally most similar, supporting each other to resist European and American nations, protect our own nation, and preserve our own culture, is this not the urgent task of the present era? Failing to do so, and 　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　, repeating the mistake of allying with the Mongols to destroy the Jin, one day if there is a change, it will not only endanger the independence of the Han nation-state but also affect the survival of Han culture." This statement is enough to show how clear the compiler's national consciousness really is.

Secondly, the first chapter of the "Introduction" of the "History of China" says: "History studies the evolution of mankind, the development of society..." This again shows that the author of this book seems to understand a bit of evolutionary viewpoint. But in reality, this large book is written entirely from an anti-evolutionary standpoint. If one truly had an evolutionary perspective, one would explain the various political and cultural changes and developments by the changes and developments of the social foundations. But the author of this book, regarding the wars between the feudal lords in the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, the learning of the various schools of thought, and the unification of Qin and its policies, regarding the well-field system implemented by Wang Mang, regarding the learning of the Song Dynasty... etc., only narrates their phenomena according to the "official histories," and does not explain the emergence, development, and decline of these phenomena from an evolutionary point of view, from the changes in the social foundation, that is, does not socially elucidate the objective significance of these phenomena. Therefore, such a large "History of China" has actually become a thing that is entirely a pile of facts, without scientific explanation, truly like a large ledger of the past several thousand years.

Of course, the main characteristic of this book is the narration of facts based on the "official histories." If it were truly a rigid narration of true historical facts, then it could perhaps serve as a kind of reference material. But many of the past historical records of China are not true. If we have no historical perspective at all and just compile a history of China based on past records, then we will make a big joke. For example, the legends of the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors, and the many myths of the various dynasties, have very little truth to them. We should deal with them with a critical attitude and should not blindly copy them from old books. However, this book, "History of China," copies the history of the Yellow Emperor, Yao, Shun, etc., as before; some of the unreasonable myths are also written in the book. Please see the following record:

"Chi You, the ruler of the Nine Li, rebelled and led his army north, seizing the Yellow River basin. Emperor Yan Yu Gang fled to Zhuolu. Xuanyuan Shi raised troops to quell the rebellion, leading the feudal lords, and fought Chi You in the wilderness of Zhuolu. Chi You could make fog, causing the soldiers to be confused. Xuanyuan made a compass chariot to show the four directions, and then captured and killed Chi You. This was the beginning of the war between the Han and Miao tribes."

We do not believe that in ancient times there was a Chi You who could make smoke bombs, "could make fog." It is natural that the invention of the compass by Xuanyuan Huangdi has a historical origin, and that this invention is also related to his war with Chi You, but this is definitely not because Chi You could make smoke bombs, "could make fog." The actual situation may have been that during the war between the Yellow Emperor and Chi You, because of changes in the climate, a thick fog arose in the air, which stimulated the Yellow Emperor to invent the compass to show the direction. This is more 　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　　It is also possible to write about the legend of Chi You being "able to make fog," but it must be critically examined with a scientific perspective and cannot be rigidly copied to mislead the reader. In fact, there are many wonderful and mysterious legends in the past history books of China. The rise and fall of each dynasty, and even the life and death of the emperors and ministers of each dynasty, as well as the order and chaos of the world, can be said to have mysterious historical explanations. If we copy them all down without criticism, wouldn't that be too ridiculous? However, the author of the "History of China" even copied the mysterious legend of Chi You being "able to make fog." This has no meaning other than showing his shallow scientific and historical knowledge.

In addition, the author of the "History of China," like the "historiographers" of the past, holds the "praise and blame" attitude of "the victor is king, the loser is bandit." Therefore, his attitude towards Tang banishing Jie, King Wu attacking Zhou, Li Yuan destroying the Sui, and Wang Mang destroying the Western Han, and the behavior of Cao Cao and Cao Pi towards Emperor Xian of Han, are completely different: he praises the former and scolds the latter. This is needless to say because the power of the former lasted longer, while the power of the latter lasted shorter. However, according to the author himself, his historical attitude is still very objective!

Although this "History of China" is already so large, it has not yet been completed; it has only been compiled to the mid-Qing Dynasty, and the history of the late Qing Dynasty and the Republic of China remains to be continued. Let's wait and see. However, for the benefit of readers, I dare not recommend this book.

Amateur Cafe

Patriotism Through Beauty 200

— Cheng

Educators all understand the slogan of learning for application.

It is said that Western blue-eyed people have a form of entertainment called "dancing." This kind of gentle exercise is said to be very beneficial to physical health and is also a common etiquette in social circles. A few years ago, so-called "song and dance performances" also appeared in our Chinese primary schools. This may have been the effect of Westernized education at the time! And at that time, it was indeed a fad. Starting with Grape Fairies, Moonlit Nights, and fine drizzles, Little Sister I Love You, from six- or seven-year-old girls who had not yet lost their infantile smell to seventeen- or eighteen-year-old girls of a delightful age, all were skilled in dancing. Therefore, when singing and dancing almost became the only teaching achievement of primary schools, the number of parent-teacher conferences and recreational activities held in schools also increased significantly. Whenever the recreational activities opened, a group of

Continued on page nine

Home
